--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / Life and career]
Taylor Alison Swift was born on December 13, 1989, in West Reading, Pennsylvania . [ 1 ] She is named after the singer-songwriter James Taylor ; [ 2 ] her parents chose a unisex name, hoping it would help her succeed in business. [ 3 ] Her father, Scott Kingsley Swift, was a stockbroker for Merrill Lynch , and her mother, Andrea Gardner Swift ( née Finlay ), worked as a mutual fund marketing executive. [ 4 ] Swift's younger brother, Austin , is an actor who manages her film projects. [ 5 ] The siblings are of Scottish, English, and German descent, with distant Irish and Italian ancestry; they are paternal great-great-grandchildren of Charles Carmine Antonio Baldi , a prominent Philadelphia businessman. [ 6 ] [ 7 ] [ 8 ] Their maternal grandmother, Marjorie Finlay ( née Moehlenkamp ), was an opera singer whose singing in church became one of Swift's earliest memories of music. [ 9 ]

During childhood, Swift spent her holiday seasons on a Christmas tree farm in Pennsylvania, [ 10 ] and summers at her family's vacation home in Stone Harbor, New Jersey , where she occasionally performed acoustic songs at a local coffee shop. [ 11 ] Raised Christian, [ 12 ] she attended preschool and kindergarten at a Montessori school run by the Bernardine Sisters of St. Francis before transferring to the Wyndcroft School in Pottstown . [ 13 ] [ 14 ] When her family moved to Wyomissing , she attended Wyomissing Area Junior/Senior High School . [ 15 ] [ 16 ] At age nine, she aspired to a career in musical theater , performing at local festivals and in Berks Youth Theatre Academy productions, [ 17 ] [ 18 ] and traveling regularly to New York City for vocal and acting lessons. [ 19 ] [ 20 ] After watching a documentary about Faith Hill , she changed her goal and became determined to pursue a country music career in Nashville, Tennessee . [ 21 ]

At the age of 11, Swift traveled to Nashville with her mother to visit record labels and submit demo tapes of Dolly Parton and Dixie Chicks karaoke covers. [ 22 ] She was rejected by all the labels, which led her to focus on songwriting. [ 23 ] She started learning the guitar at the age of 12 with the help of a computer repairman and local musician who assisted Swift in writing an original song. [ 24 ] In 2003, she and her parents started working with the talent manager Dan Dymtrow. With his help, Swift modeled for Abercrombie & Fitch , had an original song included on a Maybelline compilation CD, and was given an artist development deal from RCA Records at 13. [ 25 ] [ 26 ] To help Swift break into the country music scene, her father transferred to Merrill Lynch's Nashville office when she was 14 years old, and the family relocated to Hendersonville, Tennessee . [ 27 ] [ 28 ] Swift attended Hendersonville High School for two years before transferring to Aaron Academy, which offered homeschooling. [ 3 ] [ 29 ] [ 30 ]

Swift signed with Sony/ATV Tree Music Publishing in 2004; at 14, she became the youngest person in that publishing company's history. [ 31 ] In Nashville, she worked with experienced Music Row songwriters, including Liz Rose . [ 32 ] [ 33 ] Rose and Swift would write songs every Tuesday afternoon after school. [ 34 ] After one year on the development deal, she left RCA Records, which was planning to keep her in development until she turned 18. [ 35 ] Swift made this decision because she wanted to release the songs immediately to ensure that they still resonated with her teenage experiences. [ 36 ]

Swift organized a showcase concert at the Bluebird Cafe on November 3, 2004; among the attendees was Scott Borchetta , a music executive who was planning to establish an independent record label called Big Machine Records . [ 37 ] She signed a recording contract with Big Machine two weeks after the concert, on the condition that her albums would be self-written; [ 38 ] [ 39 ] her father purchased a three-percent stake in the company. [ 40 ] The contract was finalized by July 2005, when Swift ended her working relationship with Dymtrow. [ 41 ] She spent four months near the end of 2005 recording her debut album, Taylor Swift , with the producer Nathan Chapman . [ 42 ]

Swift's debut single, " Tim McGraw ", was released in June 2006. She and her mother spent mid-2006 sending promotional copies of the song to country radio stations across the US. [ 43 ] Taylor Swift was released on October 24, 2006. [ 44 ] On the US Billboard 200 chart, the album peaked at number five and spent 157 weeks on the chart—the longest chart run by an album in the 2000s. [ 45 ] With Taylor Swift , she became the first female country music artist to write or co-write every track on a platinum-certified debut album. [ 46 ] Swift promoted the album with a six-month radio tour and by opening for other country artists, including Rascal Flatts in 2006, [ 42 ] [ 47 ] and George Strait , [ 48 ] Brad Paisley , [ 49 ] and Tim McGraw and Faith Hill in 2007. [ 50 ] She opened for Rascal Flatts again in 2008, [ 51 ] when she dated the singer Joe Jonas . [ 52 ]

Taylor Swift was supported by four more singles in 2007 and 2008: " Teardrops on My Guitar ", " Our Song ", " Picture to Burn ", and " Should've Said No ". "Our Song" and "Should've Said No" reached number one on the Hot Country Songs chart; with the former single, Swift became the youngest person to single-handedly write and sing a number-one country single. [ 53 ] "Teardrops on My Guitar" was Swift's breakthrough single on mainstream radio and charts, reaching the top 10 of the Pop Songs , Adult Pop Songs , and Adult Contemporary charts. [ 54 ] [ 55 ] Her next releases were the Christmas extended play (EP) The Taylor Swift Holiday Collection in October 2007, [ 56 ] and the Walmart -exclusive EP Beautiful Eyes in July 2008. [ 57 ] Swift became the youngest person to be awarded with the Nashville Songwriters Association 's Songwriter/Artist of the Year in 2007. [ 58 ]

Swift's second album, Fearless , was released on November 11, 2008, in North America, [ 59 ] and in March 2009 in other markets. [ 60 ] Fearless spent eleven weeks at number one on the Billboard 200, becoming her first chart topping album and the longest-running number-one female country album; it was the best-selling album of 2009 in the US. [ 61 ] [ 62 ] The album's lead single, " Love Story ", became the first country song to top the Pop Songs chart, and its third single, " You Belong with Me ", was the first country song to top Billboard 's all-genre Radio Songs chart; [ 63 ] [ 64 ] both reached the top five of the Billboard Hot 100 chart and peaked atop the Hot Country Songs chart. [ 65 ] [ 66 ] Three other singles—" White Horse ", " Fifteen ", " Fearless "—all reached the top 10 of Hot Country Songs. [ 66 ] In 2009, Swift opened for Keith Urban 's tour and embarked on her first headlining tour, the Fearless Tour . [ 67 ]

Fearless became the most-awarded country album of all time. [ 68 ] It won the three highest awards for a country album: Album of the Year by both the Country Music Association Awards and Academy of Country Music Awards in 2009, and Best Country Album by the Grammy Awards in 2010 . [ 69 ] At the Grammys, it also won Album of the Year , and "White Horse" won Best Country Song and Best Female Country Vocal Performance . [ 70 ] Also in 2009, Swift was named Artist of the Year by both the American Music Awards and Billboard , [ 71 ] [ 72 ] and Entertainer of the Year by the Country Music Association Awards, becoming the youngest person to win the honor. [ 73 ] "You Belong with Me" won Best Female Video at the MTV Video Music Awards . Her acceptance speech was interrupted by the rapper Kanye West , an incident that became the subject of controversy and widespread media coverage. [ 74 ]

Swift featured in 2009 on " Half of My Heart " by John Mayer , with whom she was romantically linked later that year. [ 75 ] [ 76 ] She wrote " Best Days of Your Life " for Kellie Pickler , [ 77 ] co-wrote and featured on Boys Like Girls ' " Two Is Better Than One , [ 78 ] and wrote " You'll Always Find Your Way Back Home " and wrote and recorded " Crazier " for the soundtrack of Hannah Montana: The Movie , in which she also had a cameo appearance. [ 79 ] [ 80 ] She made her acting debut in the 2010 rom-com Valentine's Day and wrote " Today Was a Fairytale " for its soundtrack . [ 81 ] "Today Was a Fairytale" reached number one on the Canadian Hot 100 . [ 82 ] While shooting Valentine's Day in October 2009, Swift dated co-star Taylor Lautner . [ 83 ] She made her television debut as a rebellious teenager in a CSI: Crime Scene Investigation episode [ 84 ] and hosted and performed as the musical guest on Saturday Night Live ; she was the first host to write their own opening monologue. [ 85 ] [ 86 ]

Swift wrote her third album, Speak Now , entirely by herself. [ 87 ] Released on October 25, 2010, [ 88 ] the album debuted atop the US Billboard 200 with over one million first-week copies sold, registering the highest single-week tally for a female country artist. [ 89 ] Five of its singles—" Mine ", " Back to December ", " Mean ", " Sparks Fly ", and " Ours "—charted in the top three of Hot Country Songs; "Sparks Fly" and "Ours" reached number one. [ 66 ] "Mine" peaked at number three and was the highest-charting single on the Billboard Hot 100. [ 90 ] Swift embarked on the Speak Now World Tour from February 2011 to March 2012. [ 91 ]

In 2011, she was honored as Woman of the Year by Billboard , [ 92 ] Entertainer of the Year by both the Academy of Country Music Awards and the Country Music Association Awards, [ 93 ] and Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards. [ 94 ] She again won Entertainment of the Year by the Academy of Country Music Awards in 2012. [ 95 ] At the 54th Annual Grammy Awards in 2012, "Mean" won Best Country Song and Best Country Solo Performance . [ 96 ] After the release of Speak Now , Swift dated the actor Jake Gyllenhaal . [ 76 ]

On October 22, 2012, Swift released her fourth album, Red , [ 97 ] which featured collaborations with Chapman and new producers including Max Martin , Shellback , Dan Wilson , Jeff Bhasker , Dann Huff , and Butch Walker . [ 98 ] The album debuted at number one on the Billboard 200 with 1.21 million sales, becoming the fastest-selling country album in US history. [ 99 ] It was Swift's first number-one album in the UK. [ 100 ] During the promotion of Red , Swift was romantically involved with the political heir Conor Kennedy , and subsequently the singer Harry Styles . [ 76 ]

The two most successful singles from Red , " We Are Never Ever Getting Back Together " and " I Knew You Were Trouble ", peaked at numbers one and two on the Billboard Hot 100. [ 101 ] Both songs also reached the top five on the UK singles chart , and the former was Swift's first chart topper in the US. [ 102 ] [ 103 ] The singles " Begin Again " and " Red " peaked in the top 10 of the Billboard Hot 100, [ 65 ] while " Everything Has Changed " and " 22 " reached the top 10 on the UK singles chart. [ 102 ] The Red Tour ran from March 2013 to June 2014 and became the highest-grossing country tour with revenue of $150.2 million upon completion. [ 104 ] Swift was named Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards in 2013. [ 105 ]

Swift wrote and recorded two songs for the soundtrack album to the 2012 dystopian film The Hunger Games : "Eyes Open" and " Safe & Sound ". [ 106 ] The latter, co-written with the Civil Wars and T-Bone Burnett , won the Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media in 2013. [ 107 ] She wrote and recorded " Sweeter than Fiction " for the soundtrack to the 2013 biographical film One Chance , [ 108 ] and featured as a guest vocalist on B.o.B 's 2012 single " Both of Us " and Tim McGraw's 2013 single " Highway Don't Care ". [ 109 ] [ 110 ] Her acting roles included a voice acting role in the 2012 animated film The Lorax [ 111 ] and a supporting role in the 2014 dystopian film The Giver . [ 112 ]

Swift relocated from Nashville to New York City in March 2014 and transformed her image from country to pop with her fifth album, 1989 . [ 113 ] [ 114 ] She produced 1989 with Martin, Shellback, Chapman, and new collaborators Jack Antonoff , Imogen Heap , Ryan Tedder , and Ali Payami . [ 115 ] Released on October 27, 2014, the album spent eleven weeks at number one and one year in the top 10 of the Billboard 200. [ 116 ] [ 117 ] It has sold 14 million copies worldwide, becoming Swift's best-selling album. [ 118 ]

Three of 1989 's singles—" Shake It Off ", " Blank Space ", and " Bad Blood "—reached number one on the Billboard Hot 100; the first two made Swift the first woman to replace herself at the top spot . [ 119 ] Two other singles—" Style " and " Wildest Dreams "—peaked at numbers six and five, making 1989 the first album by Swift to have five consecutive top 10 singles on the Hot 100. [ 120 ] The 1989 World Tour was the highest-grossing tour of 2015 with $250 million in revenue. [ 121 ] She was named Billboard ' s Woman of the Year and received the inaugural Dick Clark Award for Excellence at the American Music Awards in 2014, [ 122 ] [ 123 ] and "Bad Blood" won Video of the Year and Best Collaboration at the 2015 MTV Video Music Awards . [ 124 ] At the 58th Annual Grammy Awards in 2016, 1989 made Swift the first woman to win Album of the Year twice; it also won Best Pop Vocal Album , and "Bad Blood" won Best Music Video . [ 125 ]

During the promotion of 1989 , Swift publicly opposed free music streaming services . She published an op-ed in The Wall Street Journal in July 2014 to stress the importance of albums as a creative medium for artists, [ 126 ] and, in November, removed her discography from ad-supported, free streaming platforms such as Spotify . [ 127 ] Big Machine kept her music only on paid, subscription-required platforms. [ 128 ] In a June 2015 open letter, Swift criticized Apple Music for not offering royalties to artists during its free three-month trial period and threatened to withdraw her music from the platform, [ 129 ] prompting Apple Inc. to announce that it would pay artists during the free trial period. [ 130 ] Big Machine returned Swift's catalog to Spotify and other free streaming platforms in June 2017. [ 131 ]

Swift dated the DJ Calvin Harris from March 2015 to June 2016. [ 132 ] They co-wrote the EDM single " This Is What You Came For ", which featured vocals from Rihanna ; Swift was initially credited under the pseudonym Nils Sjöberg. [ 133 ] " Better Man ", the 2016 single which Swift wrote for the country vocal group Little Big Town , won the Country Music Association Award for Song of the Year. [ 134 ] She recorded " I Don't Wanna Live Forever " with Zayn Malik for the soundtrack to the 2017 film Fifty Shades Darker ; the song became the highest-charting single from the Fifty Shades franchise on the Billboard Hot 100, peaking at number two. [ 135 ]

In April 2016, Kanye West released the single " Famous ", in which he references Swift in the line, "I made that bitch famous." Swift criticized West and said she never consented to the lyric, but West claimed that he had received her approval, and his then-wife, Kim Kardashian , released video clips of Swift and West discussing the song amicably over the phone. Although the clips were proven to be purposefully edited, [ 136 ] the controversy made Swift a subject of an online " cancel " movement, in which her critics denounced her as a fake and calculating "snake". [ 137 ] In late 2016, after briefly dating the actor Tom Hiddleston , Swift began a six-year relationship with the actor Joe Alwyn and went on hiatus. [ 138 ] [ 139 ]

In August 2017, Swift countersued and won a case against David Mueller , a former radio jockey for KYGO-FM , who sued her for damages from loss of employment. Four years earlier, she informed Mueller's employer that he had sexually assaulted her by groping her at an event. [ 140 ] Public controversies influenced Swift's sixth album, Reputation , which explores themes of fame, drama, and finding love amidst the tumultuous affairs. [ 141 ] Released on November 10, 2017, [ 142 ] Reputation opened atop the Billboard 200 with 1.21 million US sales [ 143 ] and also reached number one in Australia, [ 144 ] Canada, [ 145 ] and the UK. [ 146 ]

Reputation 's lead single, " Look What You Made Me Do ", topped the Billboard Hot 100 with the highest sales and streaming week of 2017, [ 147 ] and was Swift's first UK number-one single. [ 148 ] The singles " ...Ready for It? ", " End Game ", and " Delicate " were released to pop radio and all peaked in the top 20 of the Billboard Hot 100. [ 149 ] In 2018, Swift featured on Sugarland 's " Babe ", [ 150 ] surpassed Whitney Houston as the most-awarded female musician at the American Music Awards, [ 151 ] and embarked on the Reputation Stadium Tour , which grossed $345.7 million worldwide. [ 152 ]

In November 2018, Swift signed a record deal with Universal Music Group , which promoted her albums under Republic Records ' imprint. [ 153 ] The contract included a provision allowing Swift to maintain ownership of her master recordings . In addition, if Universal sold any part of its stake in Spotify, it agreed to distribute a non-recoupable portion of the proceeds to its artists. [ 154 ] [ 155 ]

Swift's first album with Republic Records and seventh overall, Lover , was released on August 23, 2019. [ 156 ] She produced the album with Antonoff, Louis Bell , Frank Dukes , and Joel Little . [ 157 ] Lover peaked atop the charts of such countries as Australia, Canada, Ireland, Mexico, Norway, Sweden, the UK, and the US, [ 158 ] and was the global best-selling album by a solo artist of 2019. [ 159 ] Three of its singles—" Me! ", " You Need to Calm Down ", and " Lover "—were released in 2019 and peaked in the top 10 of the Billboard Hot 100. " The Man " was released in 2020 and charted highly, and " Cruel Summer " became a resurgent success in 2023, reaching number one. [ 160 ]

In 2019, Swift was honored as Artist of the Decade by the American Music Awards and Woman of the Decade by Billboard , [ 161 ] [ 162 ] and became the first female artist to win Video of the Year for a self-directed video with "You Need to Calm Down" at the MTV Video Music Awards. [ 163 ] During the promotion of Lover , Swift became embroiled in a public dispute with the talent manager Scooter Braun after he purchased Big Machine Records, including the masters of her albums under the label. [ 164 ] Swift said that Big Machine would allow her to acquire the masters only if she exchanged one new album for each older one under a new contract, which she refused to sign. [ 164 ] In November 2020, Swift began re-recording her back catalog, which would enable her to control the licensing of her songs for commercial use . [ 165 ]

In February 2020, Swift signed a global publishing deal with Universal Music Publishing Group after her 16-year contract with Sony/ATV expired. [ 166 ] Amidst the COVID-19 pandemic in 2020, Swift surprise-released two "sister albums" that she recorded and produced with Antonoff and Aaron Dessner : Folklore on July 24, and Evermore on December 11. [ 167 ] Joe Alwyn co-wrote and co-produced several songs under the pseudonym William Bowery. [ 168 ] Both albums incorporate muted, atmospheric indie folk and indie rock sounds with orchestrations ; [ 169 ] [ 170 ] each was supported by three singles catering to US pop, country, and triple A radio formats. The singles were " Cardigan ", " Betty ", and " Exile " from Folklore , and " Willow ", " No Body, No Crime ", and " Coney Island " from Evermore . [ 171 ] Folklore and "Cardigan" made Swift the first artist to debut a number-one album and a number-one song in the same week in the US; she achieved the feat again with Evermore and "Willow". [ 172 ]

Swift won Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards in 2020 [ 173 ] and Album of the Year for Folklore at the 63rd Annual Grammy Awards in 2021, becoming the first woman to win the Grammy Award for Album of the Year three times. [ 174 ] She played Bombalurina in the film adaptation of Andrew Lloyd Webber 's musical Cats (2019), for which she co-wrote and recorded the original song " Beautiful Ghosts ". [ 175 ] The documentary Miss Americana , which chronicled parts of Swift's life and career, premiered at the 2020 Sundance Film Festival and received positive reviews. [ 176 ] [ 177 ]

Swift released two re-recorded albums in 2021: Fearless (Taylor's Version) in April and Red (Taylor's Version) in November. Both peaked atop the Billboard 200, and the former was the first re-recorded album to do so. [ 178 ] The latter helped Swift surpass Shania Twain as the female musician with the most weeks at number one on the Top Country Albums chart. [ 179 ] The song " All Too Well (Taylor's Version) " from Red (Taylor's Version) became the longest song in history to top the Billboard Hot 100. [ 180 ] [ 181 ]

Swift's tenth album, Midnights , was released on October 21, 2022. [ 182 ] Midnights was Swift's fifth album to open atop the Billboard 200 chart with US first-week sales of one million. Its tracks, led by the single " Anti-Hero ", made her the first artist to occupy the entire top 10 of the Billboard Hot 100 the same week. [ 183 ] The album peaked atop the charts of at least 14 other countries, including Australia, Canada, France, Germany, Italy, Norway, and Sweden. [ 184 ] Two other singles, " Lavender Haze " and " Karma ", both peaked at number two on the Billboard Hot 100. [ 185 ]

In 2023, Swift released two re-recorded albums: Speak Now (Taylor's Version) in July and 1989 (Taylor's Version) in October. The former broke Barbra Streisand 's record for the most number-one albums by a female artist, [ 186 ] while the latter became her 13th number-one album on the Billboard 200. [ 187 ] The single " Is It Over Now? " from 1989 (Taylor's Version) peaked at number one on the Billboard Hot 100, making Swift the first woman to have three number-one songs from three different albums in a calendar year. [ 188 ] Swift featured on Big Red Machine 's " Renegade " and "Birch" (2021), [ 189 ] Haim 's " Gasoline " (2021), [ 190 ] Ed Sheeran 's " The Joker and the Queen " (2022), [ 191 ] and the National 's " The Alcott " (2023). [ 192 ] She wrote and recorded " Carolina " for the soundtrack of the 2022 mystery film Where the Crawdads Sing , [ 193 ] and had a supporting role in the 2022 period comedy film Amsterdam . [ 194 ]

In 2022, Swift won Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards [ 195 ] and Video of the Year for All Too Well: The Short Film , her self-directed short film that accompanies "All Too Well (10 Minute Version)" at the MTV Video Music Awards; All Too Well also won the Grammy Award for Best Music Video. [ 196 ] [ 197 ] The following year, she again won the MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year with "Anti-Hero", [ 198 ] became the first musician to rank at number one on Billboard 's year-end top artists list in three different decades (2009, 2015 and 2023), [ 199 ] and had five out of the 10 best-selling albums of the year in the US, a record since Luminate began tracking US music sales in 1991. [ 200 ] At the 66th Annual Grammy Awards in 2024, Midnights made Swift the first artist to win Album of the Year four times; it also won Best Pop Vocal Album. [ 201 ]

In March 2023, Swift embarked on the Eras Tour , which she conceived as a tribute to her entire discography. The tour spanned five continents through December 2024. [ 202 ] It exerted a global cultural, economic, and political impact and culminated in an unprecedented height of popularity for Swift, [ 203 ] [ 204 ] [ 205 ] resulting in a phenomenon that the media dubbed "Swiftmania". [ 206 ] [ 207 ] The Eras Tour became the first tour to gross $1 billion in revenue and the highest-grossing tour in history , with $2 billion in total revenue. [ 208 ] Its 2023 concert film grossed $250 million, becoming the highest-grossing of its kind, [ 209 ] and its 2024 photobook sold nearly a million copies in its first week in the US, [ 210 ] followed by a 2025 documentary miniseries on Disney+ . [ 211 ] The events that happened during the tour inspired Swift's eleventh and twelfth albums, The Tortured Poets Department (2024) and The Life of a Showgirl (2025). [ 212 ] [ 213 ]

After splitting from Alwyn in April 2023, Swift dated the musician Matty Healy in May–June. [ 214 ] [ 215 ] During the run of the Eras Tour, there were controversies surrounding Ticketmaster 's monopoly that led to political scrutiny in the US , [ 216 ] venue mismanagement that led to a death in Brazil , [ 217 ] and Singapore's exclusivity deal that led to political tension in Southeast Asia. [ 218 ] In January 2024, AI-generated pornographic images portraying Swift were posted to Twitter and spread to other social media platforms, spurring criticism and demands for legal reform. [ 219 ] In July 2024, three children were killed in a stabbing attack at a Swift-themed workshop in Southport , England, leading to civil unrest in the UK . [ 220 ] The following month, the Vienna concerts were canceled following the arrest of suspects who planned a terrorist attack . [ 221 ]

The Tortured Poets Department was released on April 19, 2024. The same day, it was expanded as a double album , subtitled The Anthology . [ 222 ] It became the first album to accumulate one billion streams on Spotify in a single week and topped charts in various countries, including Australia, Canada, France, Germany, and the UK. [ 223 ] [ 224 ] In the US, it debuted atop the Billboard 200 with 2.6 million first-week units and stayed at number one for seventeen weeks, becoming Swift's longest-running chart-topping album. [ 225 ] The album was the global best-seller of 2024, with 5.6 million pure copies sold. [ 226 ] Its songs made her the first artist to monopolize the top fourteen positions of the Billboard Hot 100 the same week; [ 223 ] the lead single, " Fortnight ", peaked atop the chart, while the second single, " I Can Do It with a Broken Heart ", peaked at number three. [ 227 ] On May 30, 2025, Swift finalized the purchase of the masters to her first six original albums from Shamrock Holdings , which had acquired them from Braun in 2020. [ 228 ]

Swift began dating the football player Travis Kelce in August 2023, [ 229 ] [ 230 ] with the media dubbing them a " supercouple ". [ 231 ] [ 232 ] They became engaged in August 2025. [ 233 ] She introduced The Life of a Showgirl on his podcast New Heights that month. It was released on October 3, 2025, [ 213 ] accompanied by the promotional film Taylor Swift: The Official Release Party of a Showgirl , which topped the US box office and grossed over $50 million worldwide. [ 234 ] [ 235 ] The Life of a Showgirl debuted atop the Billboard 200 with four million first-week units—3.4 million of which were pure sales—breaking the records for the biggest debut or sales week for any album in the US . [ 236 ] It was the best-selling album globally in 2025. [ 237 ] The album's tracks occupied the top twelve spots on the Billboard Hot 100, with the lead single, " The Fate of Ophelia ", at number one; [ 238 ] it eventually became her first song to top the chart for ten cumulative weeks. [ 239 ] " Opalite ", the album's second single, also peaked at number one on the Hot 100. [ 240 ] In 2026, Swift wrote and recorded " I Knew It, I Knew You " for the animated film Toy Story 5 , marking a return to her country music roots. [ 241 ] [ 242 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / Early life]
Taylor Alison Swift was born on December 13, 1989, in West Reading, Pennsylvania . [ 1 ] She is named after the singer-songwriter James Taylor ; [ 2 ] her parents chose a unisex name, hoping it would help her succeed in business. [ 3 ] Her father, Scott Kingsley Swift, was a stockbroker for Merrill Lynch , and her mother, Andrea Gardner Swift ( née Finlay ), worked as a mutual fund marketing executive. [ 4 ] Swift's younger brother, Austin , is an actor who manages her film projects. [ 5 ] The siblings are of Scottish, English, and German descent, with distant Irish and Italian ancestry; they are paternal great-great-grandchildren of Charles Carmine Antonio Baldi , a prominent Philadelphia businessman. [ 6 ] [ 7 ] [ 8 ] Their maternal grandmother, Marjorie Finlay ( née Moehlenkamp ), was an opera singer whose singing in church became one of Swift's earliest memories of music. [ 9 ]

During childhood, Swift spent her holiday seasons on a Christmas tree farm in Pennsylvania, [ 10 ] and summers at her family's vacation home in Stone Harbor, New Jersey , where she occasionally performed acoustic songs at a local coffee shop. [ 11 ] Raised Christian, [ 12 ] she attended preschool and kindergarten at a Montessori school run by the Bernardine Sisters of St. Francis before transferring to the Wyndcroft School in Pottstown . [ 13 ] [ 14 ] When her family moved to Wyomissing , she attended Wyomissing Area Junior/Senior High School . [ 15 ] [ 16 ] At age nine, she aspired to a career in musical theater , performing at local festivals and in Berks Youth Theatre Academy productions, [ 17 ] [ 18 ] and traveling regularly to New York City for vocal and acting lessons. [ 19 ] [ 20 ] After watching a documentary about Faith Hill , she changed her goal and became determined to pursue a country music career in Nashville, Tennessee . [ 21 ]

At the age of 11, Swift traveled to Nashville with her mother to visit record labels and submit demo tapes of Dolly Parton and Dixie Chicks karaoke covers. [ 22 ] She was rejected by all the labels, which led her to focus on songwriting. [ 23 ] She started learning the guitar at the age of 12 with the help of a computer repairman and local musician who assisted Swift in writing an original song. [ 24 ] In 2003, she and her parents started working with the talent manager Dan Dymtrow. With his help, Swift modeled for Abercrombie & Fitch , had an original song included on a Maybelline compilation CD, and was given an artist development deal from RCA Records at 13. [ 25 ] [ 26 ] To help Swift break into the country music scene, her father transferred to Merrill Lynch's Nashville office when she was 14 years old, and the family relocated to Hendersonville, Tennessee . [ 27 ] [ 28 ] Swift attended Hendersonville High School for two years before transferring to Aaron Academy, which offered homeschooling. [ 3 ] [ 29 ] [ 30 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2004–2008: Career beginnings and <i>Taylor Swift</i>]
Swift signed with Sony/ATV Tree Music Publishing in 2004; at 14, she became the youngest person in that publishing company's history. [ 1 ] In Nashville, she worked with experienced Music Row songwriters, including Liz Rose . [ 2 ] [ 3 ] Rose and Swift would write songs every Tuesday afternoon after school. [ 4 ] After one year on the development deal, she left RCA Records, which was planning to keep her in development until she turned 18. [ 5 ] Swift made this decision because she wanted to release the songs immediately to ensure that they still resonated with her teenage experiences. [ 6 ]

Swift organized a showcase concert at the Bluebird Cafe on November 3, 2004; among the attendees was Scott Borchetta , a music executive who was planning to establish an independent record label called Big Machine Records . [ 7 ] She signed a recording contract with Big Machine two weeks after the concert, on the condition that her albums would be self-written; [ 8 ] [ 9 ] her father purchased a three-percent stake in the company. [ 10 ] The contract was finalized by July 2005, when Swift ended her working relationship with Dymtrow. [ 11 ] She spent four months near the end of 2005 recording her debut album, Taylor Swift , with the producer Nathan Chapman . [ 12 ]

Swift's debut single, " Tim McGraw ", was released in June 2006. She and her mother spent mid-2006 sending promotional copies of the song to country radio stations across the US. [ 13 ] Taylor Swift was released on October 24, 2006. [ 14 ] On the US Billboard 200 chart, the album peaked at number five and spent 157 weeks on the chart—the longest chart run by an album in the 2000s. [ 15 ] With Taylor Swift , she became the first female country music artist to write or co-write every track on a platinum-certified debut album. [ 16 ] Swift promoted the album with a six-month radio tour and by opening for other country artists, including Rascal Flatts in 2006, [ 12 ] [ 17 ] and George Strait , [ 18 ] Brad Paisley , [ 19 ] and Tim McGraw and Faith Hill in 2007. [ 20 ] She opened for Rascal Flatts again in 2008, [ 21 ] when she dated the singer Joe Jonas . [ 22 ]

Taylor Swift was supported by four more singles in 2007 and 2008: " Teardrops on My Guitar ", " Our Song ", " Picture to Burn ", and " Should've Said No ". "Our Song" and "Should've Said No" reached number one on the Hot Country Songs chart; with the former single, Swift became the youngest person to single-handedly write and sing a number-one country single. [ 23 ] "Teardrops on My Guitar" was Swift's breakthrough single on mainstream radio and charts, reaching the top 10 of the Pop Songs , Adult Pop Songs , and Adult Contemporary charts. [ 24 ] [ 25 ] Her next releases were the Christmas extended play (EP) The Taylor Swift Holiday Collection in October 2007, [ 26 ] and the Walmart -exclusive EP Beautiful Eyes in July 2008. [ 27 ] Swift became the youngest person to be awarded with the Nashville Songwriters Association 's Songwriter/Artist of the Year in 2007. [ 28 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2008–2010: <i>Fearless</i>]
Swift's second album, Fearless , was released on November 11, 2008, in North America, [ 1 ] and in March 2009 in other markets. [ 2 ] Fearless spent eleven weeks at number one on the Billboard 200, becoming her first chart topping album and the longest-running number-one female country album; it was the best-selling album of 2009 in the US. [ 3 ] [ 4 ] The album's lead single, " Love Story ", became the first country song to top the Pop Songs chart, and its third single, " You Belong with Me ", was the first country song to top Billboard 's all-genre Radio Songs chart; [ 5 ] [ 6 ] both reached the top five of the Billboard Hot 100 chart and peaked atop the Hot Country Songs chart. [ 7 ] [ 8 ] Three other singles—" White Horse ", " Fifteen ", " Fearless "—all reached the top 10 of Hot Country Songs. [ 8 ] In 2009, Swift opened for Keith Urban 's tour and embarked on her first headlining tour, the Fearless Tour . [ 9 ]

Fearless became the most-awarded country album of all time. [ 10 ] It won the three highest awards for a country album: Album of the Year by both the Country Music Association Awards and Academy of Country Music Awards in 2009, and Best Country Album by the Grammy Awards in 2010 . [ 11 ] At the Grammys, it also won Album of the Year , and "White Horse" won Best Country Song and Best Female Country Vocal Performance . [ 12 ] Also in 2009, Swift was named Artist of the Year by both the American Music Awards and Billboard , [ 13 ] [ 14 ] and Entertainer of the Year by the Country Music Association Awards, becoming the youngest person to win the honor. [ 15 ] "You Belong with Me" won Best Female Video at the MTV Video Music Awards . Her acceptance speech was interrupted by the rapper Kanye West , an incident that became the subject of controversy and widespread media coverage. [ 16 ]

Swift featured in 2009 on " Half of My Heart " by John Mayer , with whom she was romantically linked later that year. [ 17 ] [ 18 ] She wrote " Best Days of Your Life " for Kellie Pickler , [ 19 ] co-wrote and featured on Boys Like Girls ' " Two Is Better Than One , [ 20 ] and wrote " You'll Always Find Your Way Back Home " and wrote and recorded " Crazier " for the soundtrack of Hannah Montana: The Movie , in which she also had a cameo appearance. [ 21 ] [ 22 ] She made her acting debut in the 2010 rom-com Valentine's Day and wrote " Today Was a Fairytale " for its soundtrack . [ 23 ] "Today Was a Fairytale" reached number one on the Canadian Hot 100 . [ 24 ] While shooting Valentine's Day in October 2009, Swift dated co-star Taylor Lautner . [ 25 ] She made her television debut as a rebellious teenager in a CSI: Crime Scene Investigation episode [ 26 ] and hosted and performed as the musical guest on Saturday Night Live ; she was the first host to write their own opening monologue. [ 27 ] [ 28 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2010–2014: <i>Speak Now</i> and <i>Red</i>]
Swift wrote her third album, Speak Now , entirely by herself. [ 1 ] Released on October 25, 2010, [ 2 ] the album debuted atop the US Billboard 200 with over one million first-week copies sold, registering the highest single-week tally for a female country artist. [ 3 ] Five of its singles—" Mine ", " Back to December ", " Mean ", " Sparks Fly ", and " Ours "—charted in the top three of Hot Country Songs; "Sparks Fly" and "Ours" reached number one. [ 4 ] "Mine" peaked at number three and was the highest-charting single on the Billboard Hot 100. [ 5 ] Swift embarked on the Speak Now World Tour from February 2011 to March 2012. [ 6 ]

In 2011, she was honored as Woman of the Year by Billboard , [ 7 ] Entertainer of the Year by both the Academy of Country Music Awards and the Country Music Association Awards, [ 8 ] and Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards. [ 9 ] She again won Entertainment of the Year by the Academy of Country Music Awards in 2012. [ 10 ] At the 54th Annual Grammy Awards in 2012, "Mean" won Best Country Song and Best Country Solo Performance . [ 11 ] After the release of Speak Now , Swift dated the actor Jake Gyllenhaal . [ 12 ]

On October 22, 2012, Swift released her fourth album, Red , [ 13 ] which featured collaborations with Chapman and new producers including Max Martin , Shellback , Dan Wilson , Jeff Bhasker , Dann Huff , and Butch Walker . [ 14 ] The album debuted at number one on the Billboard 200 with 1.21 million sales, becoming the fastest-selling country album in US history. [ 15 ] It was Swift's first number-one album in the UK. [ 16 ] During the promotion of Red , Swift was romantically involved with the political heir Conor Kennedy , and subsequently the singer Harry Styles . [ 12 ]

The two most successful singles from Red , " We Are Never Ever Getting Back Together " and " I Knew You Were Trouble ", peaked at numbers one and two on the Billboard Hot 100. [ 17 ] Both songs also reached the top five on the UK singles chart , and the former was Swift's first chart topper in the US. [ 18 ] [ 19 ] The singles " Begin Again " and " Red " peaked in the top 10 of the Billboard Hot 100, [ 20 ] while " Everything Has Changed " and " 22 " reached the top 10 on the UK singles chart. [ 18 ] The Red Tour ran from March 2013 to June 2014 and became the highest-grossing country tour with revenue of $150.2 million upon completion. [ 21 ] Swift was named Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards in 2013. [ 22 ]

Swift wrote and recorded two songs for the soundtrack album to the 2012 dystopian film The Hunger Games : "Eyes Open" and " Safe & Sound ". [ 23 ] The latter, co-written with the Civil Wars and T-Bone Burnett , won the Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media in 2013. [ 24 ] She wrote and recorded " Sweeter than Fiction " for the soundtrack to the 2013 biographical film One Chance , [ 25 ] and featured as a guest vocalist on B.o.B 's 2012 single " Both of Us " and Tim McGraw's 2013 single " Highway Don't Care ". [ 26 ] [ 27 ] Her acting roles included a voice acting role in the 2012 animated film The Lorax [ 28 ] and a supporting role in the 2014 dystopian film The Giver . [ 29 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2014–2018: <i>1989</i> and <i>Reputation</i>]
Swift relocated from Nashville to New York City in March 2014 and transformed her image from country to pop with her fifth album, 1989 . [ 1 ] [ 2 ] She produced 1989 with Martin, Shellback, Chapman, and new collaborators Jack Antonoff , Imogen Heap , Ryan Tedder , and Ali Payami . [ 3 ] Released on October 27, 2014, the album spent eleven weeks at number one and one year in the top 10 of the Billboard 200. [ 4 ] [ 5 ] It has sold 14 million copies worldwide, becoming Swift's best-selling album. [ 6 ]

Three of 1989 's singles—" Shake It Off ", " Blank Space ", and " Bad Blood "—reached number one on the Billboard Hot 100; the first two made Swift the first woman to replace herself at the top spot . [ 7 ] Two other singles—" Style " and " Wildest Dreams "—peaked at numbers six and five, making 1989 the first album by Swift to have five consecutive top 10 singles on the Hot 100. [ 8 ] The 1989 World Tour was the highest-grossing tour of 2015 with $250 million in revenue. [ 9 ] She was named Billboard ' s Woman of the Year and received the inaugural Dick Clark Award for Excellence at the American Music Awards in 2014, [ 10 ] [ 11 ] and "Bad Blood" won Video of the Year and Best Collaboration at the 2015 MTV Video Music Awards . [ 12 ] At the 58th Annual Grammy Awards in 2016, 1989 made Swift the first woman to win Album of the Year twice; it also won Best Pop Vocal Album , and "Bad Blood" won Best Music Video . [ 13 ]

During the promotion of 1989 , Swift publicly opposed free music streaming services . She published an op-ed in The Wall Street Journal in July 2014 to stress the importance of albums as a creative medium for artists, [ 14 ] and, in November, removed her discography from ad-supported, free streaming platforms such as Spotify . [ 15 ] Big Machine kept her music only on paid, subscription-required platforms. [ 16 ] In a June 2015 open letter, Swift criticized Apple Music for not offering royalties to artists during its free three-month trial period and threatened to withdraw her music from the platform, [ 17 ] prompting Apple Inc. to announce that it would pay artists during the free trial period. [ 18 ] Big Machine returned Swift's catalog to Spotify and other free streaming platforms in June 2017. [ 19 ]

Swift dated the DJ Calvin Harris from March 2015 to June 2016. [ 20 ] They co-wrote the EDM single " This Is What You Came For ", which featured vocals from Rihanna ; Swift was initially credited under the pseudonym Nils Sjöberg. [ 21 ] " Better Man ", the 2016 single which Swift wrote for the country vocal group Little Big Town , won the Country Music Association Award for Song of the Year. [ 22 ] She recorded " I Don't Wanna Live Forever " with Zayn Malik for the soundtrack to the 2017 film Fifty Shades Darker ; the song became the highest-charting single from the Fifty Shades franchise on the Billboard Hot 100, peaking at number two. [ 23 ]

In April 2016, Kanye West released the single " Famous ", in which he references Swift in the line, "I made that bitch famous." Swift criticized West and said she never consented to the lyric, but West claimed that he had received her approval, and his then-wife, Kim Kardashian , released video clips of Swift and West discussing the song amicably over the phone. Although the clips were proven to be purposefully edited, [ 24 ] the controversy made Swift a subject of an online " cancel " movement, in which her critics denounced her as a fake and calculating "snake". [ 25 ] In late 2016, after briefly dating the actor Tom Hiddleston , Swift began a six-year relationship with the actor Joe Alwyn and went on hiatus. [ 26 ] [ 27 ]

In August 2017, Swift countersued and won a case against David Mueller , a former radio jockey for KYGO-FM , who sued her for damages from loss of employment. Four years earlier, she informed Mueller's employer that he had sexually assaulted her by groping her at an event. [ 28 ] Public controversies influenced Swift's sixth album, Reputation , which explores themes of fame, drama, and finding love amidst the tumultuous affairs. [ 29 ] Released on November 10, 2017, [ 30 ] Reputation opened atop the Billboard 200 with 1.21 million US sales [ 31 ] and also reached number one in Australia, [ 32 ] Canada, [ 33 ] and the UK. [ 34 ]

Reputation 's lead single, " Look What You Made Me Do ", topped the Billboard Hot 100 with the highest sales and streaming week of 2017, [ 35 ] and was Swift's first UK number-one single. [ 36 ] The singles " ...Ready for It? ", " End Game ", and " Delicate " were released to pop radio and all peaked in the top 20 of the Billboard Hot 100. [ 37 ] In 2018, Swift featured on Sugarland 's " Babe ", [ 38 ] surpassed Whitney Houston as the most-awarded female musician at the American Music Awards, [ 39 ] and embarked on the Reputation Stadium Tour , which grossed $345.7 million worldwide. [ 40 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2018–2021: <i>Lover</i>, <i>Folklore</i>, and <i>Evermore</i>]
In November 2018, Swift signed a record deal with Universal Music Group , which promoted her albums under Republic Records ' imprint. [ 1 ] The contract included a provision allowing Swift to maintain ownership of her master recordings . In addition, if Universal sold any part of its stake in Spotify, it agreed to distribute a non-recoupable portion of the proceeds to its artists. [ 2 ] [ 3 ]

Swift's first album with Republic Records and seventh overall, Lover , was released on August 23, 2019. [ 4 ] She produced the album with Antonoff, Louis Bell , Frank Dukes , and Joel Little . [ 5 ] Lover peaked atop the charts of such countries as Australia, Canada, Ireland, Mexico, Norway, Sweden, the UK, and the US, [ 6 ] and was the global best-selling album by a solo artist of 2019. [ 7 ] Three of its singles—" Me! ", " You Need to Calm Down ", and " Lover "—were released in 2019 and peaked in the top 10 of the Billboard Hot 100. " The Man " was released in 2020 and charted highly, and " Cruel Summer " became a resurgent success in 2023, reaching number one. [ 8 ]

In 2019, Swift was honored as Artist of the Decade by the American Music Awards and Woman of the Decade by Billboard , [ 9 ] [ 10 ] and became the first female artist to win Video of the Year for a self-directed video with "You Need to Calm Down" at the MTV Video Music Awards. [ 11 ] During the promotion of Lover , Swift became embroiled in a public dispute with the talent manager Scooter Braun after he purchased Big Machine Records, including the masters of her albums under the label. [ 12 ] Swift said that Big Machine would allow her to acquire the masters only if she exchanged one new album for each older one under a new contract, which she refused to sign. [ 12 ] In November 2020, Swift began re-recording her back catalog, which would enable her to control the licensing of her songs for commercial use . [ 13 ]

In February 2020, Swift signed a global publishing deal with Universal Music Publishing Group after her 16-year contract with Sony/ATV expired. [ 14 ] Amidst the COVID-19 pandemic in 2020, Swift surprise-released two "sister albums" that she recorded and produced with Antonoff and Aaron Dessner : Folklore on July 24, and Evermore on December 11. [ 15 ] Joe Alwyn co-wrote and co-produced several songs under the pseudonym William Bowery. [ 16 ] Both albums incorporate muted, atmospheric indie folk and indie rock sounds with orchestrations ; [ 17 ] [ 18 ] each was supported by three singles catering to US pop, country, and triple A radio formats. The singles were " Cardigan ", " Betty ", and " Exile " from Folklore , and " Willow ", " No Body, No Crime ", and " Coney Island " from Evermore . [ 19 ] Folklore and "Cardigan" made Swift the first artist to debut a number-one album and a number-one song in the same week in the US; she achieved the feat again with Evermore and "Willow". [ 20 ]

Swift won Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards in 2020 [ 21 ] and Album of the Year for Folklore at the 63rd Annual Grammy Awards in 2021, becoming the first woman to win the Grammy Award for Album of the Year three times. [ 22 ] She played Bombalurina in the film adaptation of Andrew Lloyd Webber 's musical Cats (2019), for which she co-wrote and recorded the original song " Beautiful Ghosts ". [ 23 ] The documentary Miss Americana , which chronicled parts of Swift's life and career, premiered at the 2020 Sundance Film Festival and received positive reviews. [ 24 ] [ 25 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2021–2023: Re-recordings and <i>Midnights</i>]
Swift released two re-recorded albums in 2021: Fearless (Taylor's Version) in April and Red (Taylor's Version) in November. Both peaked atop the Billboard 200, and the former was the first re-recorded album to do so. [ 1 ] The latter helped Swift surpass Shania Twain as the female musician with the most weeks at number one on the Top Country Albums chart. [ 2 ] The song " All Too Well (Taylor's Version) " from Red (Taylor's Version) became the longest song in history to top the Billboard Hot 100. [ 3 ] [ 4 ]

Swift's tenth album, Midnights , was released on October 21, 2022. [ 5 ] Midnights was Swift's fifth album to open atop the Billboard 200 chart with US first-week sales of one million. Its tracks, led by the single " Anti-Hero ", made her the first artist to occupy the entire top 10 of the Billboard Hot 100 the same week. [ 6 ] The album peaked atop the charts of at least 14 other countries, including Australia, Canada, France, Germany, Italy, Norway, and Sweden. [ 7 ] Two other singles, " Lavender Haze " and " Karma ", both peaked at number two on the Billboard Hot 100. [ 8 ]

In 2023, Swift released two re-recorded albums: Speak Now (Taylor's Version) in July and 1989 (Taylor's Version) in October. The former broke Barbra Streisand 's record for the most number-one albums by a female artist, [ 9 ] while the latter became her 13th number-one album on the Billboard 200. [ 10 ] The single " Is It Over Now? " from 1989 (Taylor's Version) peaked at number one on the Billboard Hot 100, making Swift the first woman to have three number-one songs from three different albums in a calendar year. [ 11 ] Swift featured on Big Red Machine 's " Renegade " and "Birch" (2021), [ 12 ] Haim 's " Gasoline " (2021), [ 13 ] Ed Sheeran 's " The Joker and the Queen " (2022), [ 14 ] and the National 's " The Alcott " (2023). [ 15 ] She wrote and recorded " Carolina " for the soundtrack of the 2022 mystery film Where the Crawdads Sing , [ 16 ] and had a supporting role in the 2022 period comedy film Amsterdam . [ 17 ]

In 2022, Swift won Artist of the Year at the American Music Awards [ 18 ] and Video of the Year for All Too Well: The Short Film , her self-directed short film that accompanies "All Too Well (10 Minute Version)" at the MTV Video Music Awards; All Too Well also won the Grammy Award for Best Music Video. [ 19 ] [ 20 ] The following year, she again won the MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year with "Anti-Hero", [ 21 ] became the first musician to rank at number one on Billboard 's year-end top artists list in three different decades (2009, 2015 and 2023), [ 22 ] and had five out of the 10 best-selling albums of the year in the US, a record since Luminate began tracking US music sales in 1991. [ 23 ] At the 66th Annual Grammy Awards in 2024, Midnights made Swift the first artist to win Album of the Year four times; it also won Best Pop Vocal Album. [ 24 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / 2023–present: The Eras Tour, <i>The Tortured Poets Department</i>, and <i>The Life of a Showgirl</i>]
In March 2023, Swift embarked on the Eras Tour , which she conceived as a tribute to her entire discography. The tour spanned five continents through December 2024. [ 1 ] It exerted a global cultural, economic, and political impact and culminated in an unprecedented height of popularity for Swift, [ 2 ] [ 3 ] [ 4 ] resulting in a phenomenon that the media dubbed "Swiftmania". [ 5 ] [ 6 ] The Eras Tour became the first tour to gross $1 billion in revenue and the highest-grossing tour in history , with $2 billion in total revenue. [ 7 ] Its 2023 concert film grossed $250 million, becoming the highest-grossing of its kind, [ 8 ] and its 2024 photobook sold nearly a million copies in its first week in the US, [ 9 ] followed by a 2025 documentary miniseries on Disney+ . [ 10 ] The events that happened during the tour inspired Swift's eleventh and twelfth albums, The Tortured Poets Department (2024) and The Life of a Showgirl (2025). [ 11 ] [ 12 ]

After splitting from Alwyn in April 2023, Swift dated the musician Matty Healy in May–June. [ 13 ] [ 14 ] During the run of the Eras Tour, there were controversies surrounding Ticketmaster 's monopoly that led to political scrutiny in the US , [ 15 ] venue mismanagement that led to a death in Brazil , [ 16 ] and Singapore's exclusivity deal that led to political tension in Southeast Asia. [ 17 ] In January 2024, AI-generated pornographic images portraying Swift were posted to Twitter and spread to other social media platforms, spurring criticism and demands for legal reform. [ 18 ] In July 2024, three children were killed in a stabbing attack at a Swift-themed workshop in Southport , England, leading to civil unrest in the UK . [ 19 ] The following month, the Vienna concerts were canceled following the arrest of suspects who planned a terrorist attack . [ 20 ]

The Tortured Poets Department was released on April 19, 2024. The same day, it was expanded as a double album , subtitled The Anthology . [ 21 ] It became the first album to accumulate one billion streams on Spotify in a single week and topped charts in various countries, including Australia, Canada, France, Germany, and the UK. [ 22 ] [ 23 ] In the US, it debuted atop the Billboard 200 with 2.6 million first-week units and stayed at number one for seventeen weeks, becoming Swift's longest-running chart-topping album. [ 24 ] The album was the global best-seller of 2024, with 5.6 million pure copies sold. [ 25 ] Its songs made her the first artist to monopolize the top fourteen positions of the Billboard Hot 100 the same week; [ 22 ] the lead single, " Fortnight ", peaked atop the chart, while the second single, " I Can Do It with a Broken Heart ", peaked at number three. [ 26 ] On May 30, 2025, Swift finalized the purchase of the masters to her first six original albums from Shamrock Holdings , which had acquired them from Braun in 2020. [ 27 ]

Swift began dating the football player Travis Kelce in August 2023, [ 28 ] [ 29 ] with the media dubbing them a " supercouple ". [ 30 ] [ 31 ] They became engaged in August 2025. [ 32 ] She introduced The Life of a Showgirl on his podcast New Heights that month. It was released on October 3, 2025, [ 12 ] accompanied by the promotional film Taylor Swift: The Official Release Party of a Showgirl , which topped the US box office and grossed over $50 million worldwide. [ 33 ] [ 34 ] The Life of a Showgirl debuted atop the Billboard 200 with four million first-week units—3.4 million of which were pure sales—breaking the records for the biggest debut or sales week for any album in the US . [ 35 ] It was the best-selling album globally in 2025. [ 36 ] The album's tracks occupied the top twelve spots on the Billboard Hot 100, with the lead single, " The Fate of Ophelia ", at number one; [ 37 ] it eventually became her first song to top the chart for ten cumulative weeks. [ 38 ] " Opalite ", the album's second single, also peaked at number one on the Hot 100. [ 39 ] In 2026, Swift wrote and recorded " I Knew It, I Knew You " for the animated film Toy Story 5 , marking a return to her country music roots. [ 40 ] [ 41 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Taylor_Swift / Artistry]
With continuous musical reinventions, [ 1 ] Swift has been described as a "musical chameleon" by journalists and music analysts. [ 2 ] [ 3 ] [ 4 ] Her discography spans styles of country, pop, and folk , [ 5 ] incorporating subgenres like country pop , [ 6 ] pop rock , [ 7 ] synth-pop , [ 8 ] country rock , electropop , and indie rock, [ 9 ] with elements of rock , rap , electronica , indie pop , and R&B . [ 10 ] [ 11 ] [ 12 ] [ 13 ] Swift self-identified as a country musician with her first four albums, [ 14 ] [ 15 ] influenced by 1990s female country artists such as Shania Twain, Faith Hill, LeAnn Rimes , and the Dixie Chicks, [ 16 ] as well as Keith Urban's incorporation of rock, pop, and blues into country music. [ 17 ] The albums feature a country pop sound defined by instruments such as the six-string banjo , mandolin , and fiddle , a slight twang in Swift's vocals, and pop rock melodies; [ 18 ] [ 19 ] Speak Now expanded this sound with 1970s and 1980s rock influences, including pop-punk and arena rock . [ 20 ] [ 21 ] Some critics argued that country signified Swift's songwriting more than her musical style, [ 7 ] [ 22 ] and accused her of causing mainstream country to stray from its roots. [ 23 ] [ 24 ]

Red 's incorporation of eclectic pop and rock styles, including Britrock , dance-pop , and dubstep , [ 25 ] [ 26 ] led to a critical debate over Swift's status as a country musician. [ 27 ] Swift then chose 1980s synth-pop to recalibrate her artistic identity, inspired by the music of Phil Collins , Annie Lennox , Peter Gabriel , and Madonna . [ 28 ] [ 29 ] 1989 , the first album in this direction, incorporates electronic arrangements consisting of dense synthesizers and drum machines . [ 30 ] Swift expanded on the electronic production on her next albums. [ 31 ] Reputation features a trap-pop production [ 32 ] [ 33 ] with elements of hip-hop, R&B, and EDM, and maximalist arrangements of heavy bass and manipulated vocals. [ 34 ] [ 35 ] [ 36 ] Lover is a pop album [ 37 ] with a 1980s-influenced sound combining dream pop , synth-pop, and pop rock. [ 38 ] [ 39 ] [ 40 ] Midnights and The Tortured Poets Department both have a minimalist synth-pop sound characterized by analog synthesizers , sustained bass notes , and simple drum machine patterns , [ 41 ] [ 42 ] although The Tortured Poets Department features a more understated production. [ 43 ] The Life of a Showgirl incorporates pop and soft rock , featuring new wave -leaning compositions and prominent acoustic guitars. [ 44 ] [ 45 ] [ 46 ] When Swift embraced a pop identity, rockist critics regarded it as an erosion of her country songwriting authenticity, [ 47 ] while others considered it necessary for her artistic evolution and defended her as a pioneer of poptimism . [ 48 ] [ 49 ]

Her 2020 albums Folklore and Evermore , described by some critics as "alternative", [ 50 ] [ 51 ] explore indie folk and rock styles. They incorporate a subtle, stripped-back soundscape with orchestrations, muted synthesizers, and drum pads . [ 52 ] [ 53 ] [ 54 ] Evermore experiments with varied song structures , asymmetric time signatures , and diverse instruments. [ 55 ] [ 56 ] Critics deemed the indie styles a mature representation of Swift's singer-songwriter status and credited her with popularizing "alternative" music, although there was disagreement over this description. [ 57 ]

Swift possesses a mezzo-soprano singing voice, [ 62 ] but she mostly sings in her alto range. [ 63 ] [ 64 ] [ 65 ] Her pitch , dialect , and accent have undergone many changes throughout her career. [ 66 ] Reviews of her early country albums criticized her vocals as weak and strained compared to those of other female country singers. [ 67 ] Defenders of Swift appreciated that she refrained from correcting her pitch with Auto-Tune and that she prioritized intimacy and emotion to communicate the messages of her songs with her audience, [ 68 ] a style that critics have described as conversational. [ 63 ] [ 69 ] According to the critic Ann Powers , this singing style is demonstrated through Swift's attention to detail, which conveys an exact feeling—"the subtle adjustment of words and phrases to suggest moods like doubt, hope, and intimacy". [ 63 ] [ 70 ]

On Red and 1989 , Swift's vocals are processed with electronic effects, such as synthesizer tweaking, looping, and multitracking, to accompany the pop production. [ 71 ] [ 63 ] Her voice on Reputation and Midnights incorporates hip-hop and R&B influences, resulting in a near- rap delivery that emphasizes rhythm and cadence over melody. [ 11 ] [ 72 ] She uses her lower register vocals extensively in Folklore [ 73 ] and both her lower and upper registers in Evermore ; the musicologist Alyssa Barca described her timbre in the upper register as "breathy and bright" and the lower register as "full and dark". [ 56 ]

Swift's vocals have received more positive assessments since Folklore . The critic Amanda Petrusich commented in 2023 that her singing had become richer, with greater clarity and a stronger tone, even in live performances. [ 74 ] Rolling Stone ranked her 102nd on their 2023 list " The 200 Greatest Singers of All Time "; the magazine argued that her breathy timbre allows for a broad range of delivery and commented: "A decade ago, including her on this list would have been a controversial move, but recent releases like Folklore , Evermore , and Midnights officially settled the argument." [ 75 ] Powers attributed Swift's vocal versatility to her evolving artistry, citing her use of hip-hop cadences and country-influenced timbre. [ 11 ]

Swift is credited as the lead songwriter on every song she has released and as the sole songwriter on over 60 tracks. [ 76 ] Her fascination with songwriting began in her childhood; she credited her mother with igniting her early interest by helping her prepare for class presentations, [ 77 ] [ 78 ] and would make up lyrics to Disney soundtrack songs once she had run out of words while singing them. [ 79 ] Her early influences included the country musicians Patsy Cline , Loretta Lynn , Tammy Wynette , and Dolly Parton; [ 80 ] [ 81 ] the singer-songwriters Joni Mitchell , Melissa Etheridge , Sarah McLachlan , and Alanis Morissette ; [ 82 ] [ 83 ] and the emo musicians Pete Wentz of Fall Out Boy and Chris Carrabba of Dashboard Confessional . [ 84 ] [ 85 ] She credited songs by the Dixie Chicks, Jeannie C. Riley , and Kenny Chesney with influencing her approach to narrative songwriting, [ 85 ] and listed Paul McCartney , Bruce Springsteen , Emmylou Harris , and Kris Kristofferson as career role models for their consistent and evolving songwriting. [ 86 ] [ 87 ]

Swift considers herself a songwriter first and foremost. [ 86 ] [ 88 ] She divides her lyrics into three types: " quill lyrics", songs rooted in antiquated poeticism; " fountain pen lyrics", based on modern and vivid storylines; and "glitter gel pen lyrics", which are lively and frivolous. [ 89 ] Using songwriting to cope with personal experiences, her songs are largely autobiographical and feature narratives that mostly revolve around love and romantic relationships. [ 90 ] [ 91 ] [ 92 ] She would start writing by identifying an emotion she wanted to convey, and the story and melody would follow. [ 93 ] Where Taylor Swift and Fearless are rooted in adolescent feelings and detail an optimistic romance inspired by fairy tales, Speak Now reflects her young adulthood, offering newfound wisdom on real-life heartbreak. [ 94 ] [ 20 ] Red explores the tumult of an intense breakup, and 1989 reflects on failed relationships with a wistful perspective; both albums incorporate lyrics that hint at sex, reflecting her personal growth. [ 64 ] Swift described Lover as a "love letter to love", inspired by her realization of "love that was very real". [ 95 ]

As her career progressed, Swift wrote about self-perception and confrontation with her critics, influenced by fame, sexism , and media scrutiny. [ 96 ] This was first exhibited in Speak Now , which set the precedent for the frantic media speculation on the subjects of her songs, specifically concerning her dating history; [ 97 ] Swift has described this practice as sexist. [ 98 ] Reputation addresses the public controversies that tarnished Swift's wholesome image while portraying a blossoming romance with intimacy and vulnerability; its extensive references to sex and alcohol marked a departure from the youthful innocence that had informed Swift's past albums. [ 34 ] [ 99 ] [ 100 ] The nocturnal ruminations of Midnights encompass regrets and fantasies informed by Swift's self-awareness of fame. [ 101 ] The Tortured Poets Department explores heartbreak and other themes to extremes: erotic desires, forbidden love, and escaping from the public spotlight. [ 12 ] [ 102 ] The Life of a Showgirl revolves around Swift's experiences during the Eras Tour, with lyrics that depict various emotions such as nostalgia, resentment, vindictiveness, and sexual arousal. [ 103 ] [ 45 ]

On Folklore and Evermore , Swift was inspired by escapism and romanticism to explore fictional narratives. [ 104 ] She imposed her emotions onto imagined characters and story arcs, inspired by authors and poets of romantic and modernist literature like F. Scott Fitzgerald , Robert Frost , William Wordsworth , and Emily Dickinson ; [ 105 ] [ 106 ] the last of whom was a distant cousin of Swift. [ 107 ] The characters on Folklore and Evermore construct their narratives from fragments of memory, symbolizing the nature of folktales and oral traditions that endure over time. [ 108 ]

Swift considers her songwriting "confessional", [ 98 ] [ 109 ] and academics have linked her style to confessional poetry , noting that her songs reference personal events and express her internal feelings to her audience. [ 92 ] [ 110 ] Critical reception of her songwriting has been largely positive, [ 86 ] [ 111 ] [ 112 ] and her melodic compositions have been highlighted for optimizing the verse-chorus form with memorable bridges . [ 63 ] [ 113 ] [ 114 ] Several scholars have credited her with taking the confessional singer-songwriter tradition to new heights, [ 115 ] [ 116 ] and journalists have variedly described her as a " poet laureate "—of puberty, [ 86 ] [ 117 ] of romance, [ 118 ] and of her generation. [ 119 ] [ 120 ] Some critics have dismissed her "confessional" style as material for tabloid gossip. [ 121 ] Objection to the perceived poetic value of her songs, mostly from rockist critics, views her as a pop star using literary subtexts as a commercial ploy, with metaphors that are at times imprecise or self-indulgent. [ 122 ]

Scholars have attributed criticisms of Swift's songwriting to sexism. The musicologist Travis Stimeling argued that while Swift's autobiographical authenticity fits country and rock standards, her mostly male detractors view her depictions of young women's experiences as trivial and unworthy of serious merit. [ 123 ] According to the English-language academic Ryan Hibbett, this gendered criticism bars Swift from receiving the artistic credentials granted to figures such as Bob Dylan , whose romantic themes and occasional literary imprecisions are not as harshly criticized. [ 124 ] In the view of the literary critic Stephanie Burt , Swift's writing is proficient at "placing inventive, evocative language into pop melodies designed to be sung". [ 125 ]

Swift's concerts feature elaborate settings that incorporate elements of Broadway theatre and high tech . [ 126 ] [ 127 ] [ 128 ] She does not rely on elaborate choreography and instead emphasizes connecting emotionally with her audience through storytelling and vocal delivery. [ 129 ] Swift has used special guests and surprise songs or covers as recurring elements of her concerts; [ 130 ] [ 131 ] the acoustic "surprise song" segment, which originated during the Speak Now World Tour, have become a fan favorite and one of the most anticipated parts of her shows. [ 132 ] [ 133 ] [ 134 ] Since 2007, she has toured with the same live band. [ 135 ] She plays four instruments live: guitar (including electric , acoustic six-string, and twelve-string ), six-string banjo, piano, and ukulele . [ 136 ] [ 137 ] [ 138 ]

Critics have praised her stage presence, stamina, [ 139 ] [ 140 ] and ability to bring forth an intimate atmosphere for her audience, even in stadium settings. [ 74 ] [ 141 ] [ 142 ] The critic Sasha Frere-Jones hailed her in 2008 as a "preternaturally skilled" entertainer who exerted professionalism with a vibrant energy. [ 22 ] The journalist Sam Lansky wrote in 2023: "Swift is many things onstage—vulnerable and triumphant, playful and sad—but the intimacy of her songcraft is front and center." [ 112 ]

Swift emphasizes visuals as a key creative component of her music. [ 143 ] She established her production company, Taylor Swift Productions , in 2008. [ 144 ] Her directorial debut was the music video for "Mine", co-directed with Roman White , in 2010; [ 145 ] and she developed the concept and treatment for "Mean" in 2011. [ 146 ] For the music videos of the 1989 and Reputation singles, she collaborated extensively with the director Joseph Kahn on eight videos; [ 147 ] among them, she produced "Bad Blood", which won Best Music Video at the Grammy Awards in 2016. [ 148 ] She worked with American Express for the "Blank Space" music video (which Kahn directed) and served as executive producer for the interactive app AMEX Unstaged: Taylor Swift Experience , for which she won a Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Interactive Program in 2015. [ 149 ]

Swift has directed 15 of her music videos . [ 150 ] [ 151 ] "The Man" was her first solo directorial work and made her the first female artist to win the MTV Video Music Award for Best Direction . [ 152 ] All Too Well: The Short Film , her filmmaking debut, made her the first artist to win the Grammy Award for Best Music Video as a solo director. [ 153 ] [ 154 ] In June 2023, Swift was invited to the Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences . [ 155 ] She has cited Joseph Kahn, Chloé Zhao , Greta Gerwig , Nora Ephron , Guillermo del Toro , John Cassavetes , and Noah Baumbach as filmmaking influences. [ 143 ] [ 156 ]

[Taylor_Swift / Songwriting]

[Taylor_Swift / Performances and stage]
Swift's concerts feature elaborate settings that incorporate elements of Broadway theatre and high tech . [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 3 ] She does not rely on elaborate choreography and instead emphasizes connecting emotionally with her audience through storytelling and vocal delivery. [ 4 ] Swift has used special guests and surprise songs or covers as recurring elements of her concerts; [ 5 ] [ 6 ] the acoustic "surprise song" segment, which originated during the Speak Now World Tour, have become a fan favorite and one of the most anticipated parts of her shows. [ 7 ] [ 8 ] [ 9 ] Since 2007, she has toured with the same live band. [ 10 ] She plays four instruments live: guitar (including electric , acoustic six-string, and twelve-string ), six-string banjo, piano, and ukulele . [ 11 ] [ 12 ] [ 13 ]

Critics have praised her stage presence, stamina, [ 14 ] [ 15 ] and ability to bring forth an intimate atmosphere for her audience, even in stadium settings. [ 16 ] [ 17 ] [ 18 ] The critic Sasha Frere-Jones hailed her in 2008 as a "preternaturally skilled" entertainer who exerted professionalism with a vibrant energy. [ 19 ] The journalist Sam Lansky wrote in 2023: "Swift is many things onstage—vulnerable and triumphant, playful and sad—but the intimacy of her songcraft is front and center." [ 20 ]
