In September 2012, Tame Impala's first U.S. feature appeared on the cover of the publication The FADER , in its 82nd issue. [ 10 ]

On 18 May 2013, it was announced via Facebook that Allbrook would leave the band to focus on other musical endeavours, and that Cam Avery of Pond and The Growl would take his place. Allbrook played his final gig with the band on their last Australian tour date of 2013 at Perth's Belvoir Amphitheatre , the same venue that Allbrook played his first gig with the band at in 2008. As a farewell gesture, the band played a cover of Outkast 's " Prototype ". [ 11 ]

Lonerism received a 2014 Grammy Award nomination in December 2013 in the Best Alternative Music Album category. [ 12 ]

"Be Above It", the first track on the album, is featured in the 2019 movie Waves . This includes the studio version, the live version from the Live Versions album and the "Erol Alkan Rework" version.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tame_Impala / 2015–2017: <i>Currents</i>]
It is believed that Parker started recording the follow-up album to Lonerism at the beginning of 2014, due to various Instagram posts that showed recording taking place at the Wave House in Western Australia , where Innerspeaker was recorded. [ 1 ] Prior to this, Parker had been touring with Tame Impala and working on other musical projects, including his disco-funk band, AAA Aardvark Getdown Services. Parker said in May 2013:

Right now, doing another album doesn't excite me. There's something narrow-minded about thinking an album is the only way you can put out music, especially in the world we're in at the moment. Anything is possible. There's so many people doing interesting things with the internet and technology, there could be so many ways of making music and listening to it. It's 2013 and you can make music anywhere... There are so many possibilities, my brain is overloading on them all. I just need to wait, think about things a bit more. Then I'll know what to do next. [ 2 ] [ 3 ]

In May 2014, Parker spoke of his growing inclination toward the recording of another album in a triple J radio interview, explaining: "I'm getting more and more sucked into the world of making an album. It's weird how it happens naturally, it's almost feels like a seasonal thing. I've started to think about tracklistings and all the things that come with an album." [ 4 ] Describing the sound of the new album, Parker said, "I'm gonna try to make it a bit more minimal this time; only use what's needed ... instead of a supreme pizza, where you just throw everything on". [ 5 ] Watson added, "[It's] probably gonna be less rock again and more electronic again, even more than the last one". [ 6 ] Parker later stated that the inspiration behind the new polished sound of Tame Impala's third album came from listening to a Fleetwood Mac song. He said that the pureness and cleanness of Fleetwood Mac's song prompted him to attempt to create a more streamlined musical style within Currents . [ 7 ]

On 6 January 2015, Spinning Top Music announced that a new Tame Impala album will be released in 2015. [ 8 ] During the same month, it was announced that the band would perform at the Boston Calling Music Festival in May 2015. [ 9 ]

On 11 March 2015, a new song titled " Let It Happen " was released as a free download. [ 10 ]

On 5 April 2015, Tame Impala announced and released the album cover for Currents in a Facebook post. A few hours later, the band released the first official single from the upcoming album on Facebook called " 'Cause I'm a Man ". [ 11 ] Later that month, on 22 April 2015, Tame Impala officially released "Let it Happen" as the second single from the album. One week later, on 29 April 2015, Kevin Parker held an AMA on Reddit , where he provoked fans to ask him to release a new song, then responding with "Disciples", which became the first promotional single for Currents . On 7 May 2015, the band announced that the album would be released on 17 July 2015 and released the third official single, " Eventually ". [ 12 ] The record ended up being the best selling one in their discography, with 1.3 million copies sold worldwide. [ 13 ]

During the same 30 April 2015 Reddit AMA, Parker said: "Up until recently, from all of Tame Impala's record sales outside of Australia I had received.... zero dollars. Someone high up spent the money before it got to me. I may never get that money." [ 14 ]

In October 2017, a collector's edition of Currents was announced. Released on 17 November, it included three B-sides and two remixes.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tame_Impala / 2018: Other projects]
By the end of 2017, Tame Impala announced that they agreed to play the 2018 Mad Cool Festival in Spain, the first live music show the band agreed to play in 2018. [ 1 ] Tame Impala also played a headline set at London's Citadel Festival in July 2018.

In March 2018, Parker worked with American rappers Travis Scott and Kanye West , as well as record producers Pharrell Williams , The Weeknd , Mike Dean , and Reine Fiske on the song " Skeletons ", which would eventually be released by Scott on his 2018 album Astroworld .

In July 2018, during an interview with Beats 1 anchor host Matt Wilkinson, Parker confirmed for the first time that he had begun working on a new Tame Impala album, adding that he was "ready to play some other songs live" and expressing an interest to headline a stage at Glastonbury Festival in 2019. He also stated that he would be "very disappointed" if the new record by Tame Impala wasn't released by summer 2019. [ 2 ]

On 1 July 2018, Tame Impala teamed up with electronic artist ZHU to create the single "My Life". [ citation needed ]

In October 2018, Parker played bass for rapper Travis Scott for a performance of "Skeletons/Astrothunder" on Saturday Night Live , with singer-songwriter John Mayer also part of the backing band. [ 3 ]

On 10 October, the band was scheduled to headline the first night of the annual Desert Daze festival in its new location in Moreno Beach, but had to cut their set short after three songs due to inclement weather. [ 4 ]

On 31 October, rapper Theophilus London released a new single in collaboration with Tame Impala under the moniker of "Theo Impala". [ 5 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tame_Impala / 2019–2022: <i>The Slow Rush</i>]
On 2 January 2019, Tame Impala was announced as a headliner for the 2019 Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival . They also headlined the 2020 Primavera Sound festival, making them only the second Australian act to do so. Around the same time, Parker announced that he expected to release a new album during that summer. [ 1 ] [ 2 ]

On 21 March 2019, Tame Impala released the single " Patience " [ 3 ] and teased new music on Instagram for the forthcoming album. [ 4 ] They were the musical guest for Saturday Night Live on 30 March, with host Sandra Oh . [ 5 ] On the show, the band performed "Patience" and a new song, " Borderline ", [ 6 ] which was released 12 April. [ 7 ] On 25 October, Tame Impala revealed the title of their fourth studio album, The Slow Rush . Three days later on 28 October, they released the song " It Might Be Time ", and on 3 December, they released the single " Posthumous Forgiveness ". The album was released on 14 February 2020 and features 12 tracks that were recorded in Los Angeles and in Parker's hometown of Fremantle, Australia. [ 8 ]

Josh Terry of Vice named Tame Impala his "Artist of the Decade" for the 2010s, writing, "No artist captured how genres cross-pollinated throughout the 2010s better than Tame Impala". He added, "In the age of streaming and the big-box festival bubble, Parker's discography seems factory-made for both a crowd of thousands and a chill night alone with a vibe-heavy playlist" and that "his music embodies the technology-driven sense of loneliness of this decade better than any of his peers". [ 9 ]

" The Less I Know the Better " was voted number one in Triple J's Hottest 100 of the Decade on 14 March 2020. This was the highest ranking for Tame Impala in a Hottest 100 Countdown and the first time the project had attained number one in any Hottest 100. (The same song had previously placed fourth in the 2015 Hottest 100.) [ 10 ]

On 20 March 2020, Parker appeared on The Weeknd's album After Hours , producing and providing background vocals on the track " Repeat After Me (Interlude) ". At the 2020 ARIA Music Awards in November, Tame Impala won a further five trophies: "Album of the Year", "Best Rock Album", Engineer of the Year" and "Producer of the Year" for The Slow Rush , as well as "Best Group". [ 11 ]

In October 2021, the band announced that a deluxe box set edition of The Slow Rush would be released in February 2022. [ 12 ]

In March 2021, the band's 2012 song "Elephant", from the album Lonerism , was covered by the Australian children's music group The Wiggles for triple j 's Like a Version segment. The Wiggles' cover version went on to place at number one in 2021's Hottest 100.

In February 2022, the band released The Slow Rush B-Sides and Remixes .

In May 2022, the band released the single " Turn Up the Sunshine ", a collaboration with Diana Ross . The track is the lead single from the Jack Antonoff -produced original soundtrack album for the film Minions: The Rise of Gru . With the exception of this track, the album primarily features new spins on classic '70s hits by artists such as Brittany Howard , St. Vincent , H.E.R. and many others. In August 2022, Gorillaz released the song " New Gold ", on which Tame Impala is featured. [ 13 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tame_Impala / 2023–present: Collaborations and <i>Deadbeat</i>]
Throughout 2023 and 2024, Tame Impala was featured in a number of collaborations and soundtracks. In March 2023, Tame Impala released the song "Wings of Time" from the soundtrack of the film Dungeons & Dragons: Honor Among Thieves . [ 1 ] In April 2023, Tame Impala collaborated with Thundercat and released "No More Lies". He assisted in songwriting, and provided guitar, vocals, drums, and keyboards. [ 2 ] For the film Barbie , Tame Impala released "Journey to the Real World", as part of the soundtrack album .

In January 2024, Tame Impala collaborated with Justice on the single " One Night/All Night " for their album Hyperdrama . On the album's release in April 2024, Tame Impala appeared on another song, " Neverender ". Parker co-wrote and produced Dua Lipa 's third studio album, Radical Optimism . He later joined Lipa onstage during her headline performance at Glastonbury 2024 , performing Tame Impala's "The Less I Know the Better" and Lipa's " Houdini ". [ 3 ]

On 15 May 2024, it was announced Sony Music Publishing had purchased the catalog of Tame Impala from Parker for an undisclosed amount, encompassing all previous and future works. [ 4 ] [ 5 ] [ 6 ] Moreover, in a mid-2024 interview with The Guardian , Parker said that work on the fifth Tame Impala album had begun, stating: "It's not finished yet, but I think it'll be [finished] soon. I'm loving how excited I am by it." [ 7 ] He had earlier reassured fans of the unreleased album's progress on Instagram with images of him at work in his studio in Los Angeles and Western Australia, the latter of which was captioned "don't worry". [ 8 ] On 28 March 2025, Parker appeared on Dua Lipa's Radical Optimism Tour as special guest performing "The Less I Know The Better" in her segment playing local songs. [ 9 ]

On 7 June 2025, Parker previewed a new song while DJing at Nitsa Club in Barcelona during Primavera Sound . He told the audience "there's no going back from this point on". [ 10 ] The song, titled " End of Summer ", and an accompanying music video were released on 25 July, with an accompanying limited edition twelve-inch vinyl single, which featured a second new song on its B-side . On 3 September and 26 September 2025 respectively, the songs " Loser " and " Dracula " were released as singles with accompanying music videos. [ 11 ] [ 12 ] Furthermore, the music video for "Loser" stars actor and musician Joe Keery . [ 13 ] On 4 September 2025, Parker announced the title and album cover for the fifth Tame Impala album, Deadbeat . [ 14 ] It was released on 17 October 2025 to polarizing reviews, featuring a more house -adjacent sound inspired by the rave scene of Western Australia. [ 15 ] [ 16 ] [ 17 ] A remix of the single "Dracula" with South Korean singer Jennie was released on 6 February 2026. [ 18 ] The viral remix became Tame Impala's first song to reach the top ten of the US Billboard Hot 100 as well as the Billboard Global 200 . [ 19 ] [ 20 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tame_Impala / Musical style]
Parker's decision to make the music for Tame Impala in the studio by himself is a result of his liking "the kind of music that is the result of one person constructing an awesome symphony of sound. You can layer your own voice 700 times for half a second if you want, and I just love that kind of music". [ 1 ] However, Parker has to translate his music to a live setting with the band, and the band doesn't play the songs until they have been recorded. "The only jamming that's done as a band is done a long time after the song is recorded for the sake of the live environment. It's good for us, because we can take a song that's been recorded and do what we want to it: slow it down, speed it up, make it 10 seconds or 10 minutes long. It gives us a lot of freedom." [ 2 ]

Some favoured and often-used effects by Parker include phasing , delay , reverb and fuzz . Experimentation with different effects pedals such as the BOSS BR600 and Moog Moogerfooger MF-105M [ 3 ] has led to Parker creating new and unique sounds. "If you make an effort to not put the pedals in the order you're meant to, then you'll end up with something new-sounding. We don't have any things that we got from another planet or anything; it's the same things everyone else has used. People have a distortion pedal and then a reverb pedal. A reverb is meant to make it sound like it's in a cathedral or something. If you put it the other way around, it won't sound like a guitar being played in a church; it'll sound like a church being stuffed inside a shoebox and then exploded. You can do different things just by treating things differently". [ 4 ]

Parker has commented on his process for making music: "I'll have a sudden, spontaneous vision of a song, have all the parts mapped out in mind, and do my best to record it as quick as I can. I'll find my eight-track and do a quick demo of just the riff, or a verse or a chorus. The song will go for like 30 seconds. I'll have a whole bunch of them [demos] and then I'll just choose which ones to make into full songs". [ 2 ] Parker has a strong sense of melody in his music, having composed "excessively melodic music from about the age of 12 to 15". [ 5 ] For Parker, the music comes before the lyrics: "I usually write the lyrics after the melody and its timing have been decided. But the words have to be meaningful. I try to synchronise certain words with the best parts of the melody, but it can be really difficult and does my head in. I like to keep the meaning pretty open and ambiguous so that it's not just me that gets something out of the lyrics. I usually write lyrics from a persona rather than tell a specific story." [ 6 ] Parker also said: "Usually I am sufficiently motivated to think of new songs every day, but I usually forget them. I seem to get an emotional kick out of sensing feelings of general desperation or hopelessness, whether it's me or someone near me or someone in a movie or anything. It's really difficult to sit down and force yourself to write a song, and that forced nature usually comes out in the song, so I just have to wait until they come to me." [ 6 ]

Tame Impala's music is heavily influenced by late 1960s and early 1970s psychedelic rock . [ 7 ] Parker has stated that he has a "fetish for extremely sugary pop music" from such artists as Britney Spears and Kylie Minogue . [ 6 ] Parker also enjoys "fucked-up explosive cosmic music" in the vein of The Flaming Lips , [ 8 ] with whom Tame Impala collaborated on the track "Children of the Moon"; the song appeared on the band's 2012 collaborative album The Flaming Lips and Heady Fwends . [ 9 ]

Combining these two things, the shoegaze band My Bloody Valentine have influenced Parker's music with their contrasting mix of abrasive guitars and ethereal melodies. He has "always been in love with the wall of sound as employed by My Bloody Valentine" and tries to capture the same "melancholy, dreamy feel" with Tame Impala. [ 10 ] Parker has elaborated on achieving a similar sonic balance in his own music: "If I was singing, I wouldn't be able to match the tone of the instruments, which is really crunchy. The instruments are quite sonically brutal, but the voice is really soft, and I think that kind of resonates with people. It's kind of like My Bloody Valentine, where it's really brutal sounding, but kind of beautiful at the same time". [ 11 ] Tame Impala live drummer Jay Watson has described Parker's music as incorporating a "shoegaze-y guitar sound, but not played in a shoegazey manner". [ 12 ]

Electronic music is another significant influence on Tame Impala's music. [ 13 ] Parker aims to incorporate the structure of electronic music into rock instrumentation: "The way we do music, it's organic, but it's meant to be quite repetitive and hypnotic, almost in a kind of electronic nature. Using our playing as though it was a living sample". [ 14 ] A sound featured prominently on Innerspeaker is a pitch-shifted guitar tone that many mistook for a synth . Parker has explained his reasoning for such production choices: "I had a few obsessions when recording Innerspeaker . One was to make the guitars sound like synths and drums sound like drum samples and pretty much anything except guitars and drums. I'm obsessed with confusing people as to the origin of a sound." [ 6 ] He has described his dream collaboration as "probably [being] someone really, really kind of fucked up", citing the electronic artists Aphex Twin and Squarepusher as examples: "You know, someone that would like scare me, but I'd be able to see how they do all their really insanely headcase stuff and I'd be able to learn from it". [ 15 ]

Parker was inspired to take up various creative endeavours at a young age: "I used to draw a lot when I was very young, and I used to get the most immense feeling of satisfaction from finishing a picture and looking back at it, even though I wasn't actually that good. When I started playing music, I got the same feeling from making a song, even if it was just a few noises or drum patterns put together. It was all about the buzz from making something from nothing. Music always affected me greatly as a listener anyway, usually from listening to music in my dad's car or listening to him play guitar". [ 6 ]

Lo-fi music is also a favourite of Parker's, and he incorporated it heavily in the early days of Tame Impala, heard prominently on the Tame Impala EP . With the release of Innerspeaker , Parker went for a different approach to a lo-fi sound, aiming more for a more cosmic and sonic wall of sound , helped by mixer Dave Fridmann . Parker explained: "It sounds more cohesive, like an organism. It has a different emotion to it; it brings out a different feeling when it's absolutely blaring at you. I love that sound." [ 2 ]

Parker has also stated that Supertramp , one of his favourite bands, are a major influence on the musical style of Tame Impala. Despite their difference in sound, he feels he is always somewhat "channeling Supertramp". [ 16 ] He has said that listening to the Bee Gees on mushrooms inspired him to change the sound of the music he was making on Currents . [ 17 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tame_Impala / Influences]
Tame Impala's music is heavily influenced by late 1960s and early 1970s psychedelic rock . [ 1 ] Parker has stated that he has a "fetish for extremely sugary pop music" from such artists as Britney Spears and Kylie Minogue . [ 2 ] Parker also enjoys "fucked-up explosive cosmic music" in the vein of The Flaming Lips , [ 3 ] with whom Tame Impala collaborated on the track "Children of the Moon"; the song appeared on the band's 2012 collaborative album The Flaming Lips and Heady Fwends . [ 4 ]

Combining these two things, the shoegaze band My Bloody Valentine have influenced Parker's music with their contrasting mix of abrasive guitars and ethereal melodies. He has "always been in love with the wall of sound as employed by My Bloody Valentine" and tries to capture the same "melancholy, dreamy feel" with Tame Impala. [ 5 ] Parker has elaborated on achieving a similar sonic balance in his own music: "If I was singing, I wouldn't be able to match the tone of the instruments, which is really crunchy. The instruments are quite sonically brutal, but the voice is really soft, and I think that kind of resonates with people. It's kind of like My Bloody Valentine, where it's really brutal sounding, but kind of beautiful at the same time". [ 6 ] Tame Impala live drummer Jay Watson has described Parker's music as incorporating a "shoegaze-y guitar sound, but not played in a shoegazey manner". [ 7 ]

Electronic music is another significant influence on Tame Impala's music. [ 8 ] Parker aims to incorporate the structure of electronic music into rock instrumentation: "The way we do music, it's organic, but it's meant to be quite repetitive and hypnotic, almost in a kind of electronic nature. Using our playing as though it was a living sample". [ 9 ] A sound featured prominently on Innerspeaker is a pitch-shifted guitar tone that many mistook for a synth . Parker has explained his reasoning for such production choices: "I had a few obsessions when recording Innerspeaker . One was to make the guitars sound like synths and drums sound like drum samples and pretty much anything except guitars and drums. I'm obsessed with confusing people as to the origin of a sound." [ 2 ] He has described his dream collaboration as "probably [being] someone really, really kind of fucked up", citing the electronic artists Aphex Twin and Squarepusher as examples: "You know, someone that would like scare me, but I'd be able to see how they do all their really insanely headcase stuff and I'd be able to learn from it". [ 10 ]

Parker was inspired to take up various creative endeavours at a young age: "I used to draw a lot when I was very young, and I used to get the most immense feeling of satisfaction from finishing a picture and looking back at it, even though I wasn't actually that good. When I started playing music, I got the same feeling from making a song, even if it was just a few noises or drum patterns put together. It was all about the buzz from making something from nothing. Music always affected me greatly as a listener anyway, usually from listening to music in my dad's car or listening to him play guitar". [ 2 ]

Lo-fi music is also a favourite of Parker's, and he incorporated it heavily in the early days of Tame Impala, heard prominently on the Tame Impala EP . With the release of Innerspeaker , Parker went for a different approach to a lo-fi sound, aiming more for a more cosmic and sonic wall of sound , helped by mixer Dave Fridmann . Parker explained: "It sounds more cohesive, like an organism. It has a different emotion to it; it brings out a different feeling when it's absolutely blaring at you. I love that sound." [ 11 ]

Parker has also stated that Supertramp , one of his favourite bands, are a major influence on the musical style of Tame Impala. Despite their difference in sound, he feels he is always somewhat "channeling Supertramp". [ 12 ] He has said that listening to the Bee Gees on mushrooms inspired him to change the sound of the music he was making on Currents . [ 13 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / Early life]
Billie Eilish Pirate Baird O'Connell [ 1 ] [ 2 ] was born in Los Angeles, California, on December 18, 2001. [ 3 ] She is the daughter of actress and teacher Maggie Baird [ 4 ] [ 5 ] and actor Patrick O'Connell, [ 6 ] both of whom are also musicians and work on Eilish's tours. [ 7 ] [ 8 ] [ 9 ] Eilish is of Irish and Scottish descent. [ 10 ] Her middle name, Eilish, was chosen by her parents while watching a documentary about Irish conjoined twins Katie and Eilish Holton [ 11 ] and was originally meant to be her first name, while Pirate was to have been her middle name. After her grandfather William Baird died while her mother was pregnant, her parents decided to name her Billie, after him. [ 1 ] She grew up in Los Angeles's Highland Park neighborhood. [ 12 ] [ 13 ] Naturally blonde , Eilish has been dyeing her hair since she was nine years old, starting with a Manic Panic shade of blue. She generally prefers it to be black, which feels most "like [her]". [ 14 ]

Eilish and her older brother Finneas were homeschooled by Baird, a decision their parents made to spend time with them and give them the freedom to pursue their interests. [ 6 ] [ 9 ] Baird taught Eilish and Finneas the basics of songwriting. [ 15 ] Eilish said her brother and mother inspired her to get into music. [ 16 ] Their parents encouraged the siblings to express themselves and explore whatever they wanted, including art, dancing, and acting. [ 7 ] [ 15 ]

Eilish started playing the ukulele at age six. She performed at talent shows and joined the Los Angeles Children's Chorus at age eight. [ 17 ] [ 15 ] [ 18 ] She wrote her first "real" song at age 11 for her mother's songwriting class. The song is about the zombie apocalypse, inspired by the television series The Walking Dead , from which she took script lines and episode titles. [ 19 ] [ 16 ] Eilish took some acting auditions, which she disliked, but she enjoyed recording background dialogue for crowd scenes and worked on the films Diary of a Wimpy Kid , Ramona and Beezus , and the X-Men series . [ 15 ] Eilish also took dance classes until 2016, when a growth plate injury ended her dance career and she focused on recording music. [ 20 ] [ 21 ] [ 17 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / Career]
In 2015, 13-year-old Eilish began working on songs with her brother Finneas, who had been writing and producing for several years and had his own band. [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 3 ] The first songs they recorded together were called "She's Broken" and "Fingers Crossed", the former written by Finneas and the latter by Eilish. "We recorded them and put them out on SoundCloud , just for fun", she recalled. [ 4 ]

On November 18, 2015, Eilish released the song " Ocean Eyes ". The track was written, mixed, and produced by Finneas, who had originally created it for his band the Slightlys before deciding it would be a better fit for Eilish's vocals. [ 3 ] [ 5 ] [ 2 ] [ 1 ] He gave it to Eilish when Fred Diaz, her dance teacher at the Revolution Dance Center, asked them to write a song for choreography. The siblings uploaded the song to SoundCloud , where Diaz could access and download it. [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 6 ] [ 7 ] The song received several hundred thousand listens in two weeks, and Finneas's manager, Danny Rukasin, reached out to him to discuss Eilish's potential. Rukasin felt she could achieve significant success with Finneas's help. [ 13 ]

In January 2016, Finneas and his manager arranged a deal in which Apple Music signed Eilish to A&R company Platoon, specializing in packaging emerging artists before they get a major-label contract. [ 11 ] [ 9 ] [ 10 ] Eilish then hired a publicist, who connected her to the luxury fashion brand Chanel , and a stylist, both of whom helped shape her image. [ 9 ] On March 24, 2016, a music video for "Ocean Eyes" directed by Megan Thompson premiered on Eilish's official YouTube channel. [ 14 ] "Ocean Eyes" and Eilish received praise and promotion from various media outlets and marketers, including radio stations and music supervisors such as Beats 1 , KCRW , BBC Radio 1 , Zane Lowe , Jason Kramer , Annie Mac , and Chris Douridas . [ 18 ] On June 23, 2016, Eilish and Finneas released " Six Feet Under " on SoundCloud as her second single. [ 19 ] A homemade music video for the song was released on June 30, 2016. [ 20 ] It was directed by Eilish and edited by her mother, Maggie Baird. [ 20 ]

In August 2016, Justin Lubliner, who had noticed Eilish's talent in 2015 when he first heard "Ocean Eyes", signed her to Darkroom and Interscope Records . [ 8 ] [ 21 ] He developed her rollout as an artist, taking inspiration from the model of hip hop artists such as Travis Scott and Chance the Rapper , not relying on one big single and focusing on creating a "persona and distinct aesthetic". [ 22 ] Darkroom and Interscope Records re-released "Six Feet Under" and "Ocean Eyes" as singles for digital download and streaming on November 17 and 18, 2016, respectively. [ 23 ] [ 24 ] On November 22, 2016, a dance performance music video for "Ocean Eyes" was uploaded to Eilish's YouTube channel. [ 25 ]

On January 14, 2017, Eilish released an EP with four remixes by Astronomyy, Blackbear , Goldhouse , and Cautious Clay for "Ocean Eyes", [ 26 ] and another EP for "Six Feet Under" featuring remixes by Blu J, Gazzo , Jerry Folk, and Aire Atlantica. [ 27 ] After the success of the "Ocean Eyes" remixes, Eilish released " Bellyache " on February 24, 2017. [ 28 ] A video for the song was released on March 22, 2017, directed by Miles and AJ. [ 29 ] Eilish released " Bored " on March 30, 2017, as part of the soundtrack to the Netflix series 13 Reasons Why . [ 30 ] A video for "Bored" was released on June 26, 2017. [ 31 ] In March of the same year, Apple Music showcased Eilish at the South by Southwest music festival. [ 11 ] [ 15 ] On June 30, 2017, Eilish released " Watch ". [ 32 ] Eilish released another single, " Copycat ", on July 14, 2017, [ 33 ] and announced the release of her debut EP, Don't Smile at Me . [ 34 ] Eilish later released " Idontwannabeyouanymore " and " My Boy ". [ 35 ] [ 36 ] On August 11, 2017, Eilish released Don't Smile at Me . [ 37 ] The EP was a sleeper hit, reaching number 14 on the US Billboard 200 . [ 38 ] Eilish embarked on the Don't Smile at Me Tour throughout October 2017 in support of her EP. [ 39 ] Eilish released " Bitches Broken Hearts " through SoundCloud on November 10, 2017. [ 40 ] [ 41 ] [ 42 ] [ 43 ]

Eilish's team worked with Spotify , which promoted her on its most popular playlist, "Today's Top Hits". [ 9 ] The Baffler described Eilish's sound as fitting into the "streambait" genre consisting of largely "mid-tempo, melancholy pop" influenced by Lana Del Rey , whose "singing style, bleakness, and... hip-hop influenced production" shaped the aesthetic. [ 44 ] [ 9 ] Eilish's commercial success expanded with her Spotify promotion. [ 9 ] In September 2017, Apple Music named Eilish their Up Next artist, which followed with a short documentary, a live session EP, and an interview with Zane Lowe on Apple Music's radio station Beats 1 . [ 45 ] That month, the live EP, Up Next Session: Billie Eilish , was released. On December 15, 2017, Eilish released her collaboration with American rapper Vince Staples , " &Burn ", a remix of her single "Watch". It was included on the expanded edition of Don't Smile at Me . [ 46 ] [ 47 ] [ 48 ] [ 49 ]

In February 2018, Eilish embarked on her second headlining concert tour, the Where's My Mind Tour , which concluded in April 2018. [ 50 ] "Bitches Broken Hearts" was re-released worldwide on March 30, 2018. [ 51 ] For Record Store Day 2018, Eilish released " Party Favor " on a pink 7-inch vinyl , along with a cover of " Hotline Bling ", by Drake , as the B-side. [ 52 ] Eilish collaborated with American singer Khalid on the single " Lovely ", which was released on April 19, 2018, and added to the soundtrack for the second season of 13 Reasons Why . [ 53 ] She released " You Should See Me in a Crown " in July 2018. [ 54 ] The same month, Eilish performed at the Mo Pop Festival . [ 55 ]

On the day of release for her single " When the Party's Over ", [ 56 ] Eilish was featured in Vanity Fair ' s "73 Questions" rapid-fire questionnaire video series by Joe Sabia , who revisited an interview from October 2017. The resulting video was a side-by-side time capsule of both interviews showing her growth in popularity over one year. [ 57 ] She signed a talent contract with Next Management for fashion and beauty endorsements in October 2018. [ 58 ] [ 59 ] She was placed on the 2018 Forbes 30 Under 30 list in November of that year, [ 60 ] [ 61 ] and released the single " Come Out and Play " in November 2018, which was written for a holiday-themed Apple Inc. commercial. [ 62 ] In early January 2019, Don't Smile at Me reached 1 billion streams on Spotify, making her the youngest artist to top 1 billion streams on a project. [ 9 ] That month, Eilish released " Bury a Friend " as the third single from her debut album When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? , [ 63 ] [ 64 ] along with " When I Was Older ", a single inspired by the 2018 film Roma , which appeared on the compilation album Music Inspired by the Film Roma . [ 65 ] [ 66 ] In February, Eilish partnered with YouTube on a documentary miniseries, "A Snippet Into Billie's Mind". [ 11 ] [ 67 ] " Wish You Were Gay ", her fourth single from the album, was released on March 4, 2019. [ 68 ]

When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? was released on March 29, 2019. [ 69 ] Spotify launched a "multi-level campaign behind the album", creating a multimedia playlist and "new product features" that Spotify said "allow for vertical video content, custom assets, and editorial storylines, all with the goal of creating more meaningful and engaging context for [Eilish's] fans." [ 11 ] In Los Angeles, Spotify set up a "pop-up enhanced album experience", which included different artwork and a "multi-sensory" experience of each track for fans. [ 11 ] The album debuted atop the Billboard 200 as well as on the UK Albums Chart , making Eilish the first artist born in the 2000s to have a number-one album in the US and the youngest female ever to have a number-one album in the United Kingdom. [ 70 ] [ 71 ] Upon the album's debut, Eilish broke the record for most simultaneously charting Hot 100 songs by a female artist, with 14, after every song from the album, excluding "Goodbye", charted on the Hot 100. [ 72 ] The fifth single from the album, " Bad Guy ", was released in conjunction with the album. [ 73 ] A remix of the song featuring Justin Bieber was released in July 2019. [ 74 ] [ 75 ] In August, "Bad Guy" peaked at number-one in the US, ending Lil Nas X 's record-breaking 19 weeks at number-one with " Old Town Road ". [ 76 ] She is the first artist born in the 2000s and the youngest artist since Lorde (with " Royals ") to have a number-one single. [ 77 ]

Eilish began her When We All Fall Asleep Tour at Coachella Festival in April 2019, [ 78 ] with the tour concluding on November 17, 2019, in Mexico City. In August 2019, she partnered with Apple Music for Music Lab: Remix Billie Eilish, part of Apple Stores ' Music Lab sessions during which fans deconstruct her song "You Should See Me In A Crown" and learn how to create their own remix on Apple devices and GarageBand . [ 79 ] [ 80 ] On September 27, 2019, Eilish announced her Where Do We Go? World Tour . [ 81 ] The tour began in Miami on March 9, 2020, and ran for two more shows on March 10 in Orlando and March 12 in Raleigh before Eilish ended the tour prematurely due to the COVID-19 pandemic . The tour was set to conclude in Jakarta on September 7. [ 82 ]

On November 7, 2019, Jack White 's Third Man Records announced that the label would release an acoustic live album of Eilish's performance from the record label's Blue Room, exclusively sold on vinyl at Third Man retail locations in Nashville , Tennessee , and Detroit, Michigan. [ 83 ] On November 13, 2019, she released her next single, " Everything I Wanted ". [ 84 ] On November 20, 2019, Eilish was nominated for six Grammy Awards , including Record of the Year and Song of the Year for " Bad Guy " as well as Album of the Year and Best New Artist . At age 17, she became the youngest artist to be nominated in all four General Field categories . [ 85 ] In the same month, Eilish was crowned 2019's Billboard Woman of the Year . [ 86 ]

On January 14, 2020, Eilish was announced as performer of the title track for the 25th installment in the James Bond film franchise , No Time to Die , [ 87 ] written and produced with her brother. With this announcement, Eilish became the youngest artist to write and perform a James Bond theme song. [ 88 ] It became the second Bond theme song to top the British official charts and the first Bond theme performed by a female artist to do so. It was also Eilish's first number-one single in the UK. [ 89 ] At the 62nd Annual Grammy Awards , she became the youngest person to win the four main Grammy categories – Best New Artist, Record of the Year, Song of the Year, and Album of the Year – in the same year. [ 90 ] [ 91 ] During the COVID-19 pandemic, Eilish and her brother performed for both iHeart Media 's Living Room Concert for America, [ 92 ] and Global Citizen 's Together at Home concert series, singing a cover of Bobby Hebb 's "Sunny" for the latter. [ 93 ] Both virtual concerts were an effort to raise awareness and funds towards fighting the disease. [ 92 ] [ 93 ] On April 10, 2020, " Ilomilo " was sent to Italian contemporary hit radio stations by Universal Music Group , as When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? ' s seventh and final single. [ 94 ] On July 30, 2020, Eilish released " My Future ", her first original release since "No Time to Die", along with an animated video. [ 95 ] In 2020, she became the youngest person to feature on the Forbes Celebrity 100 list, with earnings of $53 million. [ 96 ] In September 2020, Eilish released a collection of branded ukuleles with guitar manufacturer Fender . [ 97 ]

On October 7, 2020, Eilish announced a virtual concert titled Where Do We Go? The Livestream . Staged in Los Angeles on October 24, the performance utilised extended reality (XR) technology and featured drummer Andrew Marshall and Eilish's brother, Finneas. Ticket proceeds were used to support touring crew members affected by COVID-19 cancellations via Crew Nation. [ 98 ] In a Vanity Fair interview, Eilish said she was working on "sixteen new songs and lov[ing] them all", revealing an upcoming musical project. [ 99 ] Eilish won three Billboard Music Awards on October 24— Top Female Artist , Top Billboard 200 Album ( When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? ), and Top New Artist —out of the 12 that she was nominated for. Also that month, she announced a new single, " Therefore I Am ", which was released along with its video on November 12, 2020. [ 100 ] Eilish performed "Therefore I Am" and "My Future" at the Jingle Ball in December 2020. [ 101 ]

" Lo Vas a Olvidar ", a single featuring Rosalía as part of HBO 's Euphoria soundtrack, was released in January 2021, for the special " Fuck Anyone Who's Not a Sea Blob ". [ 102 ] On February 26, 2021, the R. J. Cutler -directed documentary film Billie Eilish: The World's a Little Blurry was released on Apple TV+ and in select movie theaters. The film was praised by critics and fans for its in-depth look at Eilish's personal life during her ascent to fame. [ 103 ] At the 63rd Annual Grammy Awards , Eilish took home two awards: Best Song Written for Visual Media for her Bond theme and Record of the Year for " Everything I Wanted ". In her acceptance speech for Record of the Year, Eilish said that Megan Thee Stallion "deserved to win", but still thanked her fans and her brother for her award. [ 104 ] In 2021, she published her personally selected comprehensive book of photographs that shared "an intimate window into her life" on and off stage, By – Billie Eilish . [ 105 ]

On April 27, 2021, Eilish announced on her Instagram account that her second album, Happier Than Ever , would be released on July 30, and the tracklist was made available on Apple Music. The album was released in various formats, including collectible vinyl and cassette colors. [ 106 ] [ 107 ] The album's release was preceded by five singles: "My Future", "Therefore I Am", " Your Power ", [ 108 ] " Lost Cause ", [ 109 ] and " NDA ", [ 110 ] and was accompanied by the title track . On December 2, 2021, Eilish announced an eco-friendly limited-edition vinyl version of Happier Than Ever made from recycled vinyl scraps. The collector's item was available only at a number of Gucci stores around the world and included Gucci-branded nail stickers designed by the brand's creative director, Alessandro Michele. [ 111 ] To further promote the album, Eilish worked with Disney+ on the concert film Happier Than Ever: A Love Letter to Los Angeles , released in September 2021, [ 112 ] [ 113 ] and embarked on the Happier Than Ever, The World Tour in February 2022, concluding it in April 2023. [ 114 ]

In June 2021, Eilish was criticized online for videos in which she mouthed the anti-Asian slur " chink " while lip-syncing the song " Fish " by Tyler, the Creator , [ 115 ] [ 116 ] while Matthew Tyler Vorce, her reported boyfriend at the time, received criticism for alleged social media posts in which he used offensive language and slurs against gay and Black people. [ 119 ] Eilish was also accused of queerbaiting after using the caption "I love girls" to promote the music video for "Lost Cause". [ 120 ] [ 121 ] [ 122 ] On June 22, she posted an apology to Instagram stories for her usage of "chink", saying that she was "appalled and embarrassed" by the video and that she was "13 or 14" at the time and did not know the slur was a derogatory term. [ 123 ] [ 124 ] She also addressed a separate video of what was viewed as her mocking an Asian accent, writing that she was actually "speaking in a silly gibberish made up voice". [ 123 ] [ 124 ] Reflecting on the events in a July 2021 interview, Eilish said: "I said so many things then that I totally don't agree with now, or think the opposite thing. The weirdest thing is how nothing ever goes away once it's on the internet ... When you're a fucking teenager, you don't really know yourself ... I didn't actually know how I really felt. So I just came up with this facade that I stuck to." [ 125 ]

Eilish started formulating ideas for her third studio album's songs with Finneas in December 2021. [ 126 ] In a July 2022 interview with Zane Lowe for Apple Music , she said she hoped to start writing the album in 2023. [ 127 ] In 2022, Eilish won the Academy Award for Best Original Song for the song " No Time to Die " from the film No Time to Die , becoming the first person born in the 21st century to win an Academy Award . [ 128 ] That same year, she became the youngest headliner to date for two festivals, specifically Glastonbury and Coachella . [ 129 ] [ 130 ] The Pixar film Turning Red was released that year, for which she and Finneas wrote three songs, " Nobody Like U ", "U Know What's Up" and "1 True Love", performed by Turning Red 's fictional boy band 4*Town. [ 131 ]

In June 2022, during her world tour's Manchester show, Eilish debuted the then-unreleased ballad "TV". The song references the overturning of Roe v. Wade , a case that made abortion a constitutional right in the US. [ 132 ] The next month, on July 21, she surprise-released the two-track EP Guitar Songs , which includes "TV" alongside "The 30th". [ 133 ] Eilish explained her decision to surprise-release the EP during the interview with Lowe. She told him that while work on her third studio album was coming soon, she refused to wait until that time to put "TV" and "The 30th" on a track list. She wanted to spread their messages to her fans as soon as possible, noting the immediacy of its lyrics: "These songs are really current for me, and they're songs that I want to have said right now." [ 134 ] Another reason was Eilish had grown tired of doing heavy, traditional promotion for upcoming music. She wanted to release songs like she had early in her career, previewing them for fans in live concerts before releasing them without much marketing. [ 135 ] [ 136 ]

Eilish worked with Apple Music to exclusively host a film of one of the Happier Than Ever tour concerts, specifically one of her shows at The O2 Arena in London. She billed the film as a way for fans who missed out on tickets to experience the tour, wanting more people to recognize her showmanship live. [ 137 ] [ 138 ] [ 139 ] Three concerts, titled Happier Than Ever, The Hometown Encore, were held at the Kia Forum in Inglewood, California , from December 13 to 16, 2022, as part of the tour. [ 140 ] [ 141 ]

In 2023, Eilish made her acting debut in the Amazon Prime Video satirical thriller series Swarm . [ 142 ] She starred as Eva, the leader of a cult inspired by NXIVM , and received positive reviews for her performance. [ 143 ] Eilish wrote the song " What Was I Made For? " for the soundtrack of the 2023 film Barbie . According to statements posted on her social media, she was inspired to write the song after seeing unfinished scenes of the movie during its production. [ 144 ] In 2024, the song won the Academy Award for Best Original Song and two Grammy Awards for Song of the Year and Best Song Written for Visual Media. It became the tenth song in history to win both an Academy Award for Best Original Song and a Grammy Award for Song of the Year, [ 145 ] and Eilish became the youngest person ever to win two Academy Awards in any category. [ 146 ]

On April 8, 2024, Eilish announced her third studio album, Hit Me Hard and Soft , which was released on May 17, 2024. [ 147 ] [ 148 ] [ 149 ] She announced a tour to support the album, Hit Me Hard and Soft: The Tour , on April 29, 2024, with concerts in North America, Oceania and Europe between September 2024 and July 2025. [ 150 ] Also in April, Eilish was announced to be the next "featured artist" inside the Fortnite spin-off game Fortnite Festival , along with an unlockable outfit in the game. [ 151 ] While on a visit to London due to the success of the recently released album in the UK, [ 152 ] Eilish appeared alongside London-based content creator Amelia Dimoldenberg on her web series Chicken Shop Date , which was dubbed as the "flirtiest episode yet", [ 153 ] and also appeared as a guest host for children's channel CBeebies ' bedtime story. [ 154 ] In August, Eilish featured on a remix of Charli XCX 's " Guess ", a song from the deluxe version of the latter's album Brat , accompanied by a video containing scenes of Eilish in a bulldozer and the pair surrounded by piles of women's underwear, which were donated to the charity I Support the Girls . [ 155 ] On August 11, 2024, Eilish performed "Birds of a Feather" on Belmont Shore, Long Beach , during the 2024 Summer Olympics closing ceremony as part of the handover to Los Angeles , which would host the Games in 2028 . [ 156 ]

In March 2026, it was reported that Eilish was in "advanced talks" to make her film acting debut as lead character Esther Greenwood in a Sarah Polley -directed adaptation of Sylvia Plath 's The Bell Jar . [ 157 ] Eilish's Hit Me Hard and Soft: The Tour (Live in 3D) concert film, which she co-directed and produced with James Cameron , was theatrically released on May 8, 2026. [ 158 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / 2015–2017: Beginnings and early recognition]
In 2015, 13-year-old Eilish began working on songs with her brother Finneas, who had been writing and producing for several years and had his own band. [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 3 ] The first songs they recorded together were called "She's Broken" and "Fingers Crossed", the former written by Finneas and the latter by Eilish. "We recorded them and put them out on SoundCloud , just for fun", she recalled. [ 4 ]

On November 18, 2015, Eilish released the song " Ocean Eyes ". The track was written, mixed, and produced by Finneas, who had originally created it for his band the Slightlys before deciding it would be a better fit for Eilish's vocals. [ 3 ] [ 5 ] [ 2 ] [ 1 ] He gave it to Eilish when Fred Diaz, her dance teacher at the Revolution Dance Center, asked them to write a song for choreography. The siblings uploaded the song to SoundCloud , where Diaz could access and download it. [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 6 ] [ 7 ] The song received several hundred thousand listens in two weeks, and Finneas's manager, Danny Rukasin, reached out to him to discuss Eilish's potential. Rukasin felt she could achieve significant success with Finneas's help. [ 13 ]

In January 2016, Finneas and his manager arranged a deal in which Apple Music signed Eilish to A&R company Platoon, specializing in packaging emerging artists before they get a major-label contract. [ 11 ] [ 9 ] [ 10 ] Eilish then hired a publicist, who connected her to the luxury fashion brand Chanel , and a stylist, both of whom helped shape her image. [ 9 ] On March 24, 2016, a music video for "Ocean Eyes" directed by Megan Thompson premiered on Eilish's official YouTube channel. [ 14 ] "Ocean Eyes" and Eilish received praise and promotion from various media outlets and marketers, including radio stations and music supervisors such as Beats 1 , KCRW , BBC Radio 1 , Zane Lowe , Jason Kramer , Annie Mac , and Chris Douridas . [ 18 ] On June 23, 2016, Eilish and Finneas released " Six Feet Under " on SoundCloud as her second single. [ 19 ] A homemade music video for the song was released on June 30, 2016. [ 20 ] It was directed by Eilish and edited by her mother, Maggie Baird. [ 20 ]

In August 2016, Justin Lubliner, who had noticed Eilish's talent in 2015 when he first heard "Ocean Eyes", signed her to Darkroom and Interscope Records . [ 8 ] [ 21 ] He developed her rollout as an artist, taking inspiration from the model of hip hop artists such as Travis Scott and Chance the Rapper , not relying on one big single and focusing on creating a "persona and distinct aesthetic". [ 22 ] Darkroom and Interscope Records re-released "Six Feet Under" and "Ocean Eyes" as singles for digital download and streaming on November 17 and 18, 2016, respectively. [ 23 ] [ 24 ] On November 22, 2016, a dance performance music video for "Ocean Eyes" was uploaded to Eilish's YouTube channel. [ 25 ]

On January 14, 2017, Eilish released an EP with four remixes by Astronomyy, Blackbear , Goldhouse , and Cautious Clay for "Ocean Eyes", [ 26 ] and another EP for "Six Feet Under" featuring remixes by Blu J, Gazzo , Jerry Folk, and Aire Atlantica. [ 27 ] After the success of the "Ocean Eyes" remixes, Eilish released " Bellyache " on February 24, 2017. [ 28 ] A video for the song was released on March 22, 2017, directed by Miles and AJ. [ 29 ] Eilish released " Bored " on March 30, 2017, as part of the soundtrack to the Netflix series 13 Reasons Why . [ 30 ] A video for "Bored" was released on June 26, 2017. [ 31 ] In March of the same year, Apple Music showcased Eilish at the South by Southwest music festival. [ 11 ] [ 15 ] On June 30, 2017, Eilish released " Watch ". [ 32 ] Eilish released another single, " Copycat ", on July 14, 2017, [ 33 ] and announced the release of her debut EP, Don't Smile at Me . [ 34 ] Eilish later released " Idontwannabeyouanymore " and " My Boy ". [ 35 ] [ 36 ] On August 11, 2017, Eilish released Don't Smile at Me . [ 37 ] The EP was a sleeper hit, reaching number 14 on the US Billboard 200 . [ 38 ] Eilish embarked on the Don't Smile at Me Tour throughout October 2017 in support of her EP. [ 39 ] Eilish released " Bitches Broken Hearts " through SoundCloud on November 10, 2017. [ 40 ] [ 41 ] [ 42 ] [ 43 ]

Eilish's team worked with Spotify , which promoted her on its most popular playlist, "Today's Top Hits". [ 9 ] The Baffler described Eilish's sound as fitting into the "streambait" genre consisting of largely "mid-tempo, melancholy pop" influenced by Lana Del Rey , whose "singing style, bleakness, and... hip-hop influenced production" shaped the aesthetic. [ 44 ] [ 9 ] Eilish's commercial success expanded with her Spotify promotion. [ 9 ] In September 2017, Apple Music named Eilish their Up Next artist, which followed with a short documentary, a live session EP, and an interview with Zane Lowe on Apple Music's radio station Beats 1 . [ 45 ] That month, the live EP, Up Next Session: Billie Eilish , was released. On December 15, 2017, Eilish released her collaboration with American rapper Vince Staples , " &Burn ", a remix of her single "Watch". It was included on the expanded edition of Don't Smile at Me . [ 46 ] [ 47 ] [ 48 ] [ 49 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / 2018–2020: <i>When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go?</i>]
In February 2018, Eilish embarked on her second headlining concert tour, the Where's My Mind Tour , which concluded in April 2018. [ 1 ] "Bitches Broken Hearts" was re-released worldwide on March 30, 2018. [ 2 ] For Record Store Day 2018, Eilish released " Party Favor " on a pink 7-inch vinyl , along with a cover of " Hotline Bling ", by Drake , as the B-side. [ 3 ] Eilish collaborated with American singer Khalid on the single " Lovely ", which was released on April 19, 2018, and added to the soundtrack for the second season of 13 Reasons Why . [ 4 ] She released " You Should See Me in a Crown " in July 2018. [ 5 ] The same month, Eilish performed at the Mo Pop Festival . [ 6 ]

On the day of release for her single " When the Party's Over ", [ 7 ] Eilish was featured in Vanity Fair ' s "73 Questions" rapid-fire questionnaire video series by Joe Sabia , who revisited an interview from October 2017. The resulting video was a side-by-side time capsule of both interviews showing her growth in popularity over one year. [ 8 ] She signed a talent contract with Next Management for fashion and beauty endorsements in October 2018. [ 9 ] [ 10 ] She was placed on the 2018 Forbes 30 Under 30 list in November of that year, [ 11 ] [ 12 ] and released the single " Come Out and Play " in November 2018, which was written for a holiday-themed Apple Inc. commercial. [ 13 ] In early January 2019, Don't Smile at Me reached 1 billion streams on Spotify, making her the youngest artist to top 1 billion streams on a project. [ 14 ] That month, Eilish released " Bury a Friend " as the third single from her debut album When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? , [ 15 ] [ 16 ] along with " When I Was Older ", a single inspired by the 2018 film Roma , which appeared on the compilation album Music Inspired by the Film Roma . [ 17 ] [ 18 ] In February, Eilish partnered with YouTube on a documentary miniseries, "A Snippet Into Billie's Mind". [ 19 ] [ 20 ] " Wish You Were Gay ", her fourth single from the album, was released on March 4, 2019. [ 21 ]

When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? was released on March 29, 2019. [ 22 ] Spotify launched a "multi-level campaign behind the album", creating a multimedia playlist and "new product features" that Spotify said "allow for vertical video content, custom assets, and editorial storylines, all with the goal of creating more meaningful and engaging context for [Eilish's] fans." [ 19 ] In Los Angeles, Spotify set up a "pop-up enhanced album experience", which included different artwork and a "multi-sensory" experience of each track for fans. [ 19 ] The album debuted atop the Billboard 200 as well as on the UK Albums Chart , making Eilish the first artist born in the 2000s to have a number-one album in the US and the youngest female ever to have a number-one album in the United Kingdom. [ 23 ] [ 24 ] Upon the album's debut, Eilish broke the record for most simultaneously charting Hot 100 songs by a female artist, with 14, after every song from the album, excluding "Goodbye", charted on the Hot 100. [ 25 ] The fifth single from the album, " Bad Guy ", was released in conjunction with the album. [ 26 ] A remix of the song featuring Justin Bieber was released in July 2019. [ 27 ] [ 28 ] In August, "Bad Guy" peaked at number-one in the US, ending Lil Nas X 's record-breaking 19 weeks at number-one with " Old Town Road ". [ 29 ] She is the first artist born in the 2000s and the youngest artist since Lorde (with " Royals ") to have a number-one single. [ 30 ]

Eilish began her When We All Fall Asleep Tour at Coachella Festival in April 2019, [ 31 ] with the tour concluding on November 17, 2019, in Mexico City. In August 2019, she partnered with Apple Music for Music Lab: Remix Billie Eilish, part of Apple Stores ' Music Lab sessions during which fans deconstruct her song "You Should See Me In A Crown" and learn how to create their own remix on Apple devices and GarageBand . [ 32 ] [ 33 ] On September 27, 2019, Eilish announced her Where Do We Go? World Tour . [ 34 ] The tour began in Miami on March 9, 2020, and ran for two more shows on March 10 in Orlando and March 12 in Raleigh before Eilish ended the tour prematurely due to the COVID-19 pandemic . The tour was set to conclude in Jakarta on September 7. [ 35 ]

On November 7, 2019, Jack White 's Third Man Records announced that the label would release an acoustic live album of Eilish's performance from the record label's Blue Room, exclusively sold on vinyl at Third Man retail locations in Nashville , Tennessee , and Detroit, Michigan. [ 36 ] On November 13, 2019, she released her next single, " Everything I Wanted ". [ 37 ] On November 20, 2019, Eilish was nominated for six Grammy Awards , including Record of the Year and Song of the Year for " Bad Guy " as well as Album of the Year and Best New Artist . At age 17, she became the youngest artist to be nominated in all four General Field categories . [ 38 ] In the same month, Eilish was crowned 2019's Billboard Woman of the Year . [ 39 ]

On January 14, 2020, Eilish was announced as performer of the title track for the 25th installment in the James Bond film franchise , No Time to Die , [ 40 ] written and produced with her brother. With this announcement, Eilish became the youngest artist to write and perform a James Bond theme song. [ 41 ] It became the second Bond theme song to top the British official charts and the first Bond theme performed by a female artist to do so. It was also Eilish's first number-one single in the UK. [ 42 ] At the 62nd Annual Grammy Awards , she became the youngest person to win the four main Grammy categories – Best New Artist, Record of the Year, Song of the Year, and Album of the Year – in the same year. [ 43 ] [ 44 ] During the COVID-19 pandemic, Eilish and her brother performed for both iHeart Media 's Living Room Concert for America, [ 45 ] and Global Citizen 's Together at Home concert series, singing a cover of Bobby Hebb 's "Sunny" for the latter. [ 46 ] Both virtual concerts were an effort to raise awareness and funds towards fighting the disease. [ 45 ] [ 46 ] On April 10, 2020, " Ilomilo " was sent to Italian contemporary hit radio stations by Universal Music Group , as When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? ' s seventh and final single. [ 47 ] On July 30, 2020, Eilish released " My Future ", her first original release since "No Time to Die", along with an animated video. [ 48 ] In 2020, she became the youngest person to feature on the Forbes Celebrity 100 list, with earnings of $53 million. [ 49 ] In September 2020, Eilish released a collection of branded ukuleles with guitar manufacturer Fender . [ 50 ]

On October 7, 2020, Eilish announced a virtual concert titled Where Do We Go? The Livestream . Staged in Los Angeles on October 24, the performance utilised extended reality (XR) technology and featured drummer Andrew Marshall and Eilish's brother, Finneas. Ticket proceeds were used to support touring crew members affected by COVID-19 cancellations via Crew Nation. [ 51 ] In a Vanity Fair interview, Eilish said she was working on "sixteen new songs and lov[ing] them all", revealing an upcoming musical project. [ 52 ] Eilish won three Billboard Music Awards on October 24— Top Female Artist , Top Billboard 200 Album ( When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go? ), and Top New Artist —out of the 12 that she was nominated for. Also that month, she announced a new single, " Therefore I Am ", which was released along with its video on November 12, 2020. [ 53 ] Eilish performed "Therefore I Am" and "My Future" at the Jingle Ball in December 2020. [ 54 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / 2021–2022: <i>Happier Than Ever</i>]
" Lo Vas a Olvidar ", a single featuring Rosalía as part of HBO 's Euphoria soundtrack, was released in January 2021, for the special " Fuck Anyone Who's Not a Sea Blob ". [ 1 ] On February 26, 2021, the R. J. Cutler -directed documentary film Billie Eilish: The World's a Little Blurry was released on Apple TV+ and in select movie theaters. The film was praised by critics and fans for its in-depth look at Eilish's personal life during her ascent to fame. [ 2 ] At the 63rd Annual Grammy Awards , Eilish took home two awards: Best Song Written for Visual Media for her Bond theme and Record of the Year for " Everything I Wanted ". In her acceptance speech for Record of the Year, Eilish said that Megan Thee Stallion "deserved to win", but still thanked her fans and her brother for her award. [ 3 ] In 2021, she published her personally selected comprehensive book of photographs that shared "an intimate window into her life" on and off stage, By – Billie Eilish . [ 4 ]

On April 27, 2021, Eilish announced on her Instagram account that her second album, Happier Than Ever , would be released on July 30, and the tracklist was made available on Apple Music. The album was released in various formats, including collectible vinyl and cassette colors. [ 5 ] [ 6 ] The album's release was preceded by five singles: "My Future", "Therefore I Am", " Your Power ", [ 7 ] " Lost Cause ", [ 8 ] and " NDA ", [ 9 ] and was accompanied by the title track . On December 2, 2021, Eilish announced an eco-friendly limited-edition vinyl version of Happier Than Ever made from recycled vinyl scraps. The collector's item was available only at a number of Gucci stores around the world and included Gucci-branded nail stickers designed by the brand's creative director, Alessandro Michele. [ 10 ] To further promote the album, Eilish worked with Disney+ on the concert film Happier Than Ever: A Love Letter to Los Angeles , released in September 2021, [ 11 ] [ 12 ] and embarked on the Happier Than Ever, The World Tour in February 2022, concluding it in April 2023. [ 13 ]

In June 2021, Eilish was criticized online for videos in which she mouthed the anti-Asian slur " chink " while lip-syncing the song " Fish " by Tyler, the Creator , [ 14 ] [ 15 ] while Matthew Tyler Vorce, her reported boyfriend at the time, received criticism for alleged social media posts in which he used offensive language and slurs against gay and Black people. [ 18 ] Eilish was also accused of queerbaiting after using the caption "I love girls" to promote the music video for "Lost Cause". [ 19 ] [ 20 ] [ 21 ] On June 22, she posted an apology to Instagram stories for her usage of "chink", saying that she was "appalled and embarrassed" by the video and that she was "13 or 14" at the time and did not know the slur was a derogatory term. [ 22 ] [ 23 ] She also addressed a separate video of what was viewed as her mocking an Asian accent, writing that she was actually "speaking in a silly gibberish made up voice". [ 22 ] [ 23 ] Reflecting on the events in a July 2021 interview, Eilish said: "I said so many things then that I totally don't agree with now, or think the opposite thing. The weirdest thing is how nothing ever goes away once it's on the internet ... When you're a fucking teenager, you don't really know yourself ... I didn't actually know how I really felt. So I just came up with this facade that I stuck to." [ 24 ]

Eilish started formulating ideas for her third studio album's songs with Finneas in December 2021. [ 25 ] In a July 2022 interview with Zane Lowe for Apple Music , she said she hoped to start writing the album in 2023. [ 26 ] In 2022, Eilish won the Academy Award for Best Original Song for the song " No Time to Die " from the film No Time to Die , becoming the first person born in the 21st century to win an Academy Award . [ 27 ] That same year, she became the youngest headliner to date for two festivals, specifically Glastonbury and Coachella . [ 28 ] [ 29 ] The Pixar film Turning Red was released that year, for which she and Finneas wrote three songs, " Nobody Like U ", "U Know What's Up" and "1 True Love", performed by Turning Red 's fictional boy band 4*Town. [ 30 ]

In June 2022, during her world tour's Manchester show, Eilish debuted the then-unreleased ballad "TV". The song references the overturning of Roe v. Wade , a case that made abortion a constitutional right in the US. [ 31 ] The next month, on July 21, she surprise-released the two-track EP Guitar Songs , which includes "TV" alongside "The 30th". [ 32 ] Eilish explained her decision to surprise-release the EP during the interview with Lowe. She told him that while work on her third studio album was coming soon, she refused to wait until that time to put "TV" and "The 30th" on a track list. She wanted to spread their messages to her fans as soon as possible, noting the immediacy of its lyrics: "These songs are really current for me, and they're songs that I want to have said right now." [ 33 ] Another reason was Eilish had grown tired of doing heavy, traditional promotion for upcoming music. She wanted to release songs like she had early in her career, previewing them for fans in live concerts before releasing them without much marketing. [ 34 ] [ 35 ]

Eilish worked with Apple Music to exclusively host a film of one of the Happier Than Ever tour concerts, specifically one of her shows at The O2 Arena in London. She billed the film as a way for fans who missed out on tickets to experience the tour, wanting more people to recognize her showmanship live. [ 36 ] [ 37 ] [ 38 ] Three concerts, titled Happier Than Ever, The Hometown Encore, were held at the Kia Forum in Inglewood, California , from December 13 to 16, 2022, as part of the tour. [ 39 ] [ 40 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / 2023–present: <i>Hit Me Hard and Soft</i> and acting debut]
In 2023, Eilish made her acting debut in the Amazon Prime Video satirical thriller series Swarm . [ 1 ] She starred as Eva, the leader of a cult inspired by NXIVM , and received positive reviews for her performance. [ 2 ] Eilish wrote the song " What Was I Made For? " for the soundtrack of the 2023 film Barbie . According to statements posted on her social media, she was inspired to write the song after seeing unfinished scenes of the movie during its production. [ 3 ] In 2024, the song won the Academy Award for Best Original Song and two Grammy Awards for Song of the Year and Best Song Written for Visual Media. It became the tenth song in history to win both an Academy Award for Best Original Song and a Grammy Award for Song of the Year, [ 4 ] and Eilish became the youngest person ever to win two Academy Awards in any category. [ 5 ]

On April 8, 2024, Eilish announced her third studio album, Hit Me Hard and Soft , which was released on May 17, 2024. [ 6 ] [ 7 ] [ 8 ] She announced a tour to support the album, Hit Me Hard and Soft: The Tour , on April 29, 2024, with concerts in North America, Oceania and Europe between September 2024 and July 2025. [ 9 ] Also in April, Eilish was announced to be the next "featured artist" inside the Fortnite spin-off game Fortnite Festival , along with an unlockable outfit in the game. [ 10 ] While on a visit to London due to the success of the recently released album in the UK, [ 11 ] Eilish appeared alongside London-based content creator Amelia Dimoldenberg on her web series Chicken Shop Date , which was dubbed as the "flirtiest episode yet", [ 12 ] and also appeared as a guest host for children's channel CBeebies ' bedtime story. [ 13 ] In August, Eilish featured on a remix of Charli XCX 's " Guess ", a song from the deluxe version of the latter's album Brat , accompanied by a video containing scenes of Eilish in a bulldozer and the pair surrounded by piles of women's underwear, which were donated to the charity I Support the Girls . [ 14 ] On August 11, 2024, Eilish performed "Birds of a Feather" on Belmont Shore, Long Beach , during the 2024 Summer Olympics closing ceremony as part of the handover to Los Angeles , which would host the Games in 2028 . [ 15 ]

In March 2026, it was reported that Eilish was in "advanced talks" to make her film acting debut as lead character Esther Greenwood in a Sarah Polley -directed adaptation of Sylvia Plath 's The Bell Jar . [ 16 ] Eilish's Hit Me Hard and Soft: The Tour (Live in 3D) concert film, which she co-directed and produced with James Cameron , was theatrically released on May 8, 2026. [ 17 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / Artistry]
Eilish grew up listening to the Beatles , Justin Bieber , Green Day , [ 1 ] the 1975 , [ 2 ] Arctic Monkeys , Nine Inch Nails , [ 3 ] Linkin Park [ 4 ] and Lana Del Rey . [ 5 ] She has named the Beatles as her greatest musical inspiration, crediting the band for inspiring "95% of [her] love for music". [ 6 ] She has said that stumbling upon Aurora 's " Runaway " on YouTube inspired her to pursue a music career. [ 7 ] Hip hop is her favorite genre of music. [ 8 ]

She has recounted that Matty Healy was an early inspiration for her: "His show is the second show I ever went to in my life. He changed so much about who I am, how I write music." [ 2 ] [ 9 ] She has also cited Tyler, the Creator , Childish Gambino , and Avril Lavigne as major musical and style influences. [ 10 ] [ 11 ] Other influences include Adele , [ 12 ] Earl Sweatshirt , James Blake , Amy Winehouse , the Spice Girls , Lorde , Marina , Britney Spears , Nicki Minaj , XXXTentacion , and Twenty One Pilots . [ 21 ] She has also shown appreciation for Paramore after inviting Hayley Williams to join her set during Williams's first Coachella set to perform an acoustic version of " Misery Business " and sing "Happier Than Ever". [ 22 ] Eilish also named Rihanna as an inspiration for her style choices after she called fashion her "defense mechanism" during an acceptance speech. [ 23 ] She has also credited Damon Albarn for changing the way she views art and music creation. [ 24 ]

Eilish has been compared in the media to Lavigne, Lorde and Del Rey, [ 25 ] [ 26 ] [ 27 ] the last of whom she says she does not want to be compared to, saying, "That woman has made her brand so perfect for her whole career and she shouldn't have to hear that." [ 28 ] Eilish said that Ariana Grande 's 2019 album Thank U, Next inspired her to continue making music. [ 29 ]

Eilish has a soprano vocal range. [ 33 ] Avery Stone of Vice called her vocals "ethereal", [ 32 ] and Maura Johnston of Rolling Stone characterized them as "whispery". [ 34 ] Doreen St. Félix of The New Yorker wrote that she has a "husky, slurring voice that she can thin out to reedy". [ 35 ] Music critic Robert Christgau wrote that while Eilish is musically and commercially pop, her brand also "reminds us how amorphous [pop] has become", calling her soprano "too diminutive for vocal calisthenics" and adding that her "playful version of teen- goth angst" and " electro -saturated debut album" captivate a diverse audience. [ 36 ] Her music is generally described as pop [ 37 ] [ 38 ] and alternative pop , [ 39 ] [ 40 ] [ 41 ] although she also incorporates elements of electronic , [ 38 ] [ 42 ] alternative, dance , [ 38 ] hip-hop , and rock . [ 42 ] Her musical style has primarily been categorized as alternative pop , [ 43 ] [ 44 ] electropop , [ 42 ] [ 45 ] and indie pop , [ 42 ] [ 46 ] while also falling under bedroom pop , [ 47 ] emo pop , [ 48 ] experimental pop , [ 49 ] pop rock , [ 50 ] and teen pop labels, [ 51 ] with dark pop and indie electronic inflections. [ 42 ] She has delved into downtempo and jazz pop styles on her sophomore album Happier Than Ever (2021). [ 52 ] [ 53 ] Musicologist Jessica Holmes argued that much of Eilish's music concerns her depression. [ 54 ]

Eilish and her brother, Finneas, collaborate on songwriting. [ 55 ] [ 56 ] Finneas writes for Eilish's albums, produces her music, and also performs in live shows. [ 57 ] [ 55 ] Eilish and Finneas "like to completely make up things and become characters" and "have songs that are really fictional". [ 56 ] Eilish said a number of the songs also derive from her and Finneas' experiences. [ 56 ] They try to write "really interesting and conversational" lyrics: "We try to say stuff that doesn't have to be that deep [...] but you say something way deeper in a certain way that makes sense, but you haven't really thought about." [ 56 ] Finneas has said that when he writes for his sister, he aims to "write [songs] that I think she'll relate to and enjoy singing and empathise with the lyrics and make her own". [ 58 ] When he writes with Eilish, he tries "to help her tell whatever story she's trying to tell, bounce ideas off of her, listen to her ideas", and use a language that fits her voice telling the story. [ 58 ]

In later interviews, Eilish described becoming more emotionally "honest" and pushing herself out of her comfort zone during the songwriting process. [ 59 ] While discussing Hit Me Hard and Soft with Zane Lowe for Apple Music , she said that early sessions for the album involved unfinished song fragments that were later revisited and developed into completed songs, which was a new approach for their musical process. [ 59 ] Eilish said she came to enjoy songwriting more during the album's creation, and also described the record as pushing herself vocally more than any of her previous albums. [ 59 ]

Eilish had wanted to direct her own music videos since age 14 but was initially not given the opportunity due to lack of experience. [ 60 ] In 2019, she made her directorial debut with the video for her song " Xanny ". [ 61 ] She has since directed nearly all of her music videos, including " Happier Than Ever ", " What Was I Made For? ", and " Chihiro ". [ 62 ] [ 63 ] [ 64 ]

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Billie_Eilish / Influences]
Eilish grew up listening to the Beatles , Justin Bieber , Green Day , [ 1 ] the 1975 , [ 2 ] Arctic Monkeys , Nine Inch Nails , [ 3 ] Linkin Park [ 4 ] and Lana Del Rey . [ 5 ] She has named the Beatles as her greatest musical inspiration, crediting the band for inspiring "95% of [her] love for music". [ 10 ] [ 11 ] Other influences include Adele , [ 12 ] Earl Sweatshirt , James Blake , Amy Winehouse , the Spice Girls , Lorde , Marina , Britney Spears , Nicki Minaj , XXXTentacion , and Twenty One Pilots .
